 **विदूषकः—** (परिक्रम्य ससम्भ्रमम्) बकुलावलिके एष बालाशोकवृक्षस्य पल्लवानि लङ्घयति हरिणः। एहि निवारयाव एनम्। **(ङ)**

** राजा—** वयस्य एवमेवास्मिन्रक्षणक्षणेऽवहितेन त्वया भवितव्यम्।

 **बकुला॰—** तथा। (इति प्रस्थिता।) **(च)**

** विदूषकः—** एवमपि गौतमः सन्दिश्यते। **(छ)**

** बकुला॰—** (परिक्रम्य) आर्य गौतम, अहमप्रकाशे तिष्ठामि। त्वं द्वाररक्षको भव। **(ज)**

** विदूषकः—** युज्यते। **(झ)**

(निष्क्रान्ता बकुलावलिका।)

 **विदू॰—** इदं तावत्स्फटिकस्थलमाश्रितो भवामि। (तथा कृत्वा) अहो सुखस्पर्शता शिलाविशेषस्य। (इति निद्रायते।) **(ञ)**  
\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) सहि बहुसो किल भट्टा विप्पलद्धो। दाणिं दाव अत्ता विस्ससणिज्जो करीअदु। (ख) सहि मह उण मन्दभग्गाए सिविणसमाअमो वि भट्टिणो दुल्लहो आसि। (ग) भट्टा केहेदु से उत्तरम्। (घ) अणुगहीदम्ह। (ङ) बउलावलिए एसो बालासोअरुक्खस्स पल्लवाइं लङ्घेदि हरिणो। एहि णिवारेम णम्। (च) तह। (छ) एव्वं वि गोदमो सन्दिसेअदि। (ज) अज्ज गोदम अहम् अप्पआसे चिट्ठामि। तुमं दुवाररक्खओ होहि। (झ) जुज्जइ। (ञ) इमं दाव फलिहत्थलम् अस्सिदो होमि। अहो सुहष्फरिसदा सिलाविनेसस्स।

———————————————————————————————

(मालविका ससाध्वसं तिष्ठति।)

 **राजा—**

**विसृज सुन्दरि सङ्गमसाध्वसं  
 तव चिरात्प्रभृति प्रणयोन्मुखे।  
परिगृहाण गते सहकारतां  
 त्वमतिमुक्तलताचरितं मयि॥१३॥**

 **माल॰—** देव्या भयेनात्मनः प्रियं कर्तुं न पारयामि। **(क)**

 **राजा—** अयि न भेतव्यम्।

 **माल॰—** (सोपालम्भम्) यो न बिभेति स मया भट्टिनीदर्शने दृष्टसामर्थ्यो भर्ता।

 **राजा—**

**दाक्षिण्यं नाम बिम्बोष्ठि बैम्बिकानां कुलव्रतम्।  
तन्मे दीर्घाक्षि ये प्राणास्ते त्वदाशानिबन्धनाः॥१४॥**

तदनुगृह्यतां चिरानुरक्तोऽयं जनः। (इति सङ्क्षेपमभिनयति।)

(मालविका नाट्येन परिहरति।)

 **राजा—** (आत्मगतम्) रमणीयः खलु नवाङ्गनानां मदनविषयव्यापारः। तथा हि।

**हस्तं कम्पवती रुणद्धि रशनाव्यापारलोलाङ्गुलिं-  
 हस्तौ स्वौ नयति स्तनावरणतामालिङ्ग्यमाना बलात्।  
पातुं पक्ष्मलचक्षुरुन्नमयतः साचीकरोत्याननं  
 व्याजेनाप्यभिलाषपूरणसुखं निर्वर्तयत्येव मे॥१५॥**

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) देवीए भएण अत्तणो पिअं कादुं ण पारेमि। (ख) जो ण भाअदि सो मए भट्टिणीदंसणे दिठ्ठिसमत्थो भट्टा।

———————————————————————————————

(ततः प्रविशतीरावती निपुणिका च।)

 **इरावती—** हञ्जे निपुणिके सत्यं त्वं परिगतार्था चन्द्रिकया समुद्रगृहालिन्दे शयित एकाकी आर्यगौतमो दृष्ट इति। **(क)**

** निपुणिका—** अन्यथा कथं भट्टिन्यै विज्ञापयामि। **(ख)**

** इरावती—** तेन हि तत्रैव गच्छामः संशयान्मुक्तमार्यपुत्रस्य प्रियवयस्यं प्रष्टुं च। **(ग)**

** निपुणिका—** सावशेषमिव भट्टिन्या वचनम्। **(घ)**

** इरावती—** चित्रगतमार्यपुत्रं प्रसादयितुं च। **(ङ)**

** निपुणिका—** अथ कथमिदानीं भर्ता एव न प्रसाद्यते। **(च)**

** इरावती—** मुग्धे यादृशश्चित्रगतस्तादृश एवान्यसङ्क्रान्तहृदय आर्यपुत्रः। केवलमुपचारातिक्रमं प्रमार्जितुमयमारम्भः। **(छ)**

** निपुणिका—** इत इतो भट्टिनी। **(ज)**

(उभे परिक्रामतः)

(प्रविश्य)

 **चेटी—** जयतु भट्टिनी। देवी भणति। न मे एष मत्सरस्य कालः। तेन खलु तव बहुमानं वर्धयितुं वयस्यया सह निगडबन्धने कृता मालविका। यद्यनुमन्यस आर्यपुत्रस्य प्रियं कर्तुं तथा करोमि।  
\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) हज्जे णिउणिए सच्चं तुमं परिगदत्था चन्दिआए समुद्दघरअलिन्दे सइदो एआई अज्जगोदमो दिठ्ठोत्ति। (ख) अण्णहा कहं भट्ठिणीए विण्णावेमि।(ग) तेण हि तहिम् एव्व गच्छामो संसआदो मुत्तम् अज्जउत्तस्स पिअवअस्सं पुच्छिदुं सावसेसं विअ भट्टिणीए वअणम्। (ङ) चित्तगदम् अज्जउत्तं पसादेदुम् अ। (च) अह कहं दाणिं भट्ठा एव्व ण प्पसादीअदि। (छ) मुद्धे जारिसो चित्तगदो तारिसो एव्व अण्णसङ्कन्तहिअओ अज्जउत्तो। केवलम् उवआरादिक्कमं पमज्जिदुम् अअम् आरम्भो ! (ज) इदो इदो भट्टिणी।

———————————————————————————————

यत्तवेष्टं तन्मे भणेति। **(क)**

** इरावती—** नागरिके विज्ञापय देवीम्। का वयं भट्टिनीं नियोजयितुम्। परिजननिगडनेन दर्शितो मय्यनुग्रहः। कस्य वान्यस्य प्रसादेनायं जनो वर्धत इति। **(ख)**

** चेटी— **तथा। (इति निष्क्रान्ता।)

 **निपुणिका—** (परिक्रम्यावलोक्य च) भट्टिनि एष द्वारदेशे समुद्रगृहस्य विपरिणगत इव बलीवर्द आर्यगौतम आसीन एव निद्रायते।

 **इरावती—** अत्याहितम्। न खलु सावशेषो विषविकारो भवेत्। **(ङ)**

** निपुणिका—** प्रसन्नमुखवर्णो दृश्यते। अपि च ध्रुवसिद्धिना चिकित्सितः। तदस्याशङ्कनीयं पापम्। **(च)**

** विदूषकः—** (उत्स्वप्नायते) भवति मालविके— **(छ)**

** निपुणिका—** श्रुतं भट्टिन्या। कस्यैष आत्मनीनो हताशः कितवः। सर्वकालमित एव स्वस्तिवाचनमोदकैः कुक्षिं पूरयित्वा साम्प्रतं मालविकामुत्स्वप्नायते। **(ज)**  
\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) जेदु भट्टिणी। देवी भणादि। ण मे एसो मच्छरस्स कालो। तुह खु बहुमाणं वड्डेदुं वअस्मिआए सह णिअलबन्धणे किदा मालविआ। जइ अणुमण्णसि अज्जउत्तस्स पिअं कादुं तहा करेमि। जं तुह इच्छिअं तं मे भणाहित्ति ! (ख) गाअरिए विण्णावेहि देविम्। का वअं भट्टिणिं णिओजेदुम्। परिअणणिअलणेण दंसिदो मइ अणुग्गहो। कस्स वा अण्णस्स पसादेण अअं जणो वट्टदित्ति। (ग) तह। (घ) भट्टिणि एसो दुवारदेसे समुद्दधरस्स विपणिगदो विअ बलीवद्दो अज्जगोदमो आसीणो एव्व णिद्दाअदि। (ङ) अच्चाहिदम्। ण खु सावसेसो विसविआरो हवे। (च) पसण्णमुहवण्णो दीसइ। अवि अ धुवसिद्धिणा चिइच्छिदो। ता से असङ्कणिज्जं पावम्। (छ) भोदि मालविए। (ज) सुदं भट्टिणीए। कस्स एसो अत्तणीणो हदासो किदवो। सव्वकालम् इदो एव्व सोत्थिवाअणमोदएहिं कुर्च्छि पूरिअ सम्पदं मालविअम् उस्सिविणावेदि।

———————————————————————————————

 **विदूषकः—** इरावतीमतिक्रामन्ती भव। **(क)**

** निपुणिका—** एतदत्याहितम्। इमं भुजङ्गभीरुकं ब्रह्मबन्धुमनेन भुजङ्गकुटिलेन दण्डकाष्ठेन स्तम्भान्तरिता भाययिष्यामि। **(ख)**

** इरावती—** अर्हत्येव कृतघ्न उपद्रवस्य। **(ग)**

(निपुणिका विदूषकस्योपरि दण्डकाष्टं पातयति।)

 **विदूषकः—** (सहसा प्रबुध्य) अविधा अविधा। भो वयस्य सर्पो म उपरि पतितः। **(घ)**

 **राजा—** (सहसोपसृत्य) सखे न भेतव्यं न भेतव्यम्।

 **माल॰— **(अनुसृत्य) भर्तः मा तावत्सहसा निष्क्राम। सर्प इति भण्यते। **(ङ)**

 **इरा॰—** हा धिक् हा धिक्। भर्ता इत एव धावति। **(च)**

** विदू॰— **(सप्रहासम्) कथं दण्डकाष्ठमेतत्। अहं पुनर्जाने यन्मया केतकीकण्टकैर्दंशं कृत्वा सर्पस्य इव दंशः कृतस्तन्मे फलित। **(छ)**

(प्रविश्य पटाक्षेपेण)

 **बकुला॰— **मा तावद्भर्ता प्रविशतु। इह कुटिलगतिः सर्प इव दृश्यते। **(ज)**

** इरा॰—** (स्तम्भान्तरिता राजानमुपेत्य) अपि निर्विघ्नमनोरथो दिवासङ्केतो मिथुनस्य। **(झ)**

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) इरावदिम् अदिक्कमन्ती होहि। (ख) एदम् अच्चाहिदम्। इमं भुअङ्गभीरुअं बह्मबन्धुम् इमिणा भुअङ्गकुडिलेण दण्डकट्टेण खम्भन्तरिदा भाअइस्सम्। (ग) अरुहदि एव्व किदग्घो उवद्दवस्स। (घ) अविहा अविहा। भो वअस्स सप्पो मे उपरि पडिदो। (ङ) भट्टा मा दाव सहसा णिक्कम। सप्पोत्ति भणीअदि। (च) हद्धि हद्धि। भट्टा इदो एव्व धावदि। (छ) कहं दण्डकठ्ठम् एदम्। अहम् उण जाणे जं मए केदहङ्कण्टएहि दंसं करिअ सप्पस्स इव दंसो किदो तं मे फलिदन्ति। (ज) मा दाव भट्टा पविसदु। इह कुडिलगइं सप्पो विअ दीसदि। (झ) अवि णिव्विग्घमणोरहो दिवासङ्केदो मिहुणस्स।

———————————————————————————————

(सर्वे इरावतीं द्वष्ट्वा सम्भ्रान्ताः।)

 **राजा—** प्रिये अपूर्वोऽयमुपचारः।

 **इराव॰—** बकुलावलिके दिष्ट्या दूत्याधिकारविषया सम्पूर्णा ते प्रतिज्ञा। **(क)**

** बकुला॰—** प्रसीदतु भट्टिनी। किं नु खलु दर्दुरा व्याहरन्तीति देवः पृथिवीं विस्मरति। **(ख)**

** विदू॰—** मा तावत्। भवत्या दर्शनमात्रेणात्रभवान्प्रणिपातलङ्घनं विस्मृतः। भवती पुनरद्यापि प्रसादं न गृह्णाति। **(ग)**

** इरा॰—** कुपितेदानीमहं किं करिष्यामि। **(घ)**

** राजा—** अस्थाने कोप इत्यनुपपन्नं त्वयि। तथा हि

**कदा मुखं वरतनु कारणदृते  
 तवागतं क्षणमपि कोपपात्रताम्।  
अपर्वणि ग्रहकलुषेन्दुमण्डला  
 विभावरी कथय कथं भविष्यति॥१६॥**

** इरा॰— **अस्थान इति सुष्ठु व्याहृतमार्यपुत्रेण। अन्यसङ्क्रान्तेषु अस्माकं भागधेयेषु यदि पुनः कुप्येयं ततो हास्या भवेयम्। **(ङ)**

** राजा—** त्वमन्यथा कल्पयसि। अहं पुनः सत्यमेव कोपस्थानं न पश्यामि। कुतः।  
\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) बउलावलिए दिट्ठिआ दुच्चाहिआरविसआ सम्पुण्णा दे पडिण्णा। (ख) पसीददु भट्टिणी। किं णु खु दद्दुरा वाहरन्तित्ति देवो पुढवीं विसुमरदि। (ग) मा दाव। होदीए दंसणमत्तेण अत्तभवं पणिवादलङ्घणं विसुमरिदो। होदी उण अञ्जवि पसादं ण गेण्हेदि। (घ) कुविदा दाणिम् अह किं करिस्सम्। (ङ) अठ्ठाणेत्ति सुट्ठु वाहरिदम् अज्जउत्तेण। अण्णसङ्कन्तेसु अह्माणं भाअहेएसु जदि उण कुप्पेअं तदि हस्सा भवेअम्।

———————————————————————————————

**नार्हति कृतापराधोऽप्युत्सवदिवसेषु परिजनो बन्धम्।  
इति मोचिते मयैते प्रणिपतितुं मामुपगते च॥१७॥**

 **इरावती—** निपुणिके गच्छ देवीं विज्ञापय। दृष्टो भवत्याः पक्षपातो नन्वद्येति। **(क)**

** निपुणिका—** तथा। (इति निष्क्रान्ता।) **(ख)**

** विदूषकः—** (आत्मगतम्) अहो अनर्थः सम्पतितः। बन्धनभ्रष्टो गृहकपोतो चिल्लाया मुखे पतितः। **(ग)**

(प्रविश्य)

** निपुणिका—** (अपवार्य) भट्टिनि यदृच्छादृष्ट्या माधविकया आख्यातम्। एवं खल्वेतन्निर्वृत्तमिति। (इति कर्णे कथयति।) **(घ)**

** इरावती—** (आत्मगतम्) उपपन्नम्। सत्यमयमत्र ब्रह्मबन्धुना कृतः प्रयोगः। (विदूषकं विलोक्य प्रकाशम्) इयमस्य कामतन्त्रसचिवस्य नीतिः। **(ङ)**

** विदूषकः—** भवति यदि नीतेरेकमप्यक्षरं पठेयं तदा गायत्रीमपि विस्मरेयम्। **(च)**

** राजा—** (आत्मगतम्) कथं नु खल्वस्मात्सङ्कटादात्मानं मोचयिष्यामि।

(प्रविश्य)

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) णिउणिए गच्छ। देवीं विण्णावेहि। दिठ्ठो भवदीए पक्खवादो णम् अज्जति। (ख) तह। (ग) अहो अणत्थो सम्पडिदो। बन्धणटभट्टो गिहकवोदो चिल्लाए मुहे पडिदो। (घ) भट्टिणि जदिच्छादिट्टाए माहविआए आचक्खिदम्। एव्वं खु एदं णिव्वुत्तन्ति। (ङ) उववण्णम्। सच्चम् अअम् एत्थ बम्हबन्धुणा किदो पओओ। इअँ इमस्स कामतन्तसचिवस्स णीदी। (च) भोदि जदि णीदिए एक्कंवि अक्खरं पढेअं तदो गाअत्तिं वि विसुमरेअम्।

———————————————————————————————

 **जयसेना—** (सावेगम्) देव कुमारी वसुलक्ष्मीः कन्दुकमनुधावन्ती पिङ्गलवनारेण बलवत्त्रासिताङ्कनिषण्णा देव्याः प्रवातकिसलयमिव वेपमाना न किमपि प्रकृतिं प्रतिपद्यते। **(क)**

** राजा—** कष्टम्। कातरो वालभावः।

 **इरावती—** (सावेगम्) त्वरतामार्यपुत्र एनां समाश्वासयितुम्। मास्याः सन्त्रासजनितो विकारो वर्धताम्। **(ख)**

** राजा—** अयमेनां सञ्ज्ञापयामि (इति सत्वरं परिक्रामति।)

 **विदूषकः—** (आत्मगतम्) साधु रे पिङ्गलवानर। साधु परित्रातस्त्वया सङ्कटात् स्वपक्षः। **(ग)**

(निष्क्रान्तः सवयस्यो राजा इरावती निपुणिका प्रतीहारी च।)

 **मालविका—** सखि देवीं चिन्तयित्वा वेपते मे हृदयम्। न जानेऽतः परं किं वानुभवितव्यं भविष्यतीति। **(घ)**

(नेपथ्ये)

 आश्चर्यमाश्चर्यम्। अपूर्ण एव पञ्चरात्रे दोहदस्य मुकुलैः सन्नद्धस्तपनीयाशोकः। यावद्देव्यै निवेदयामि। **(ङ)**

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) देव कुमारी वसुलच्छी कन्दुअम् अणुधावन्ती पिङ्गलवाणरेण वलिअँ तासिदा अङ्कणिसण्णा देवीए पवादकिसलअं विअ वेवमाणा ण किंवि पकिदिं पडिवज्जइ। (ख) तुवरदु अज्जउत्तो णं समस्सासइदुम्। मा से सन्तासजणिदो विआरो वड्ढदु। (ग) साहु रे पिङ्गलवाणर। साहु परित्तादो तुए सङ्कटादो सपक्खो। (घ) हला देविं चिन्तिअ वेवदि मे हिअअम्। ण जाणे अदो वरं किं वा अणुहविदव्वं हविस्सदित्ति। (ङ) अच्चरिअम् अच्चरिअम्। अपुण्णे एव्व पञ्चरत्ते दोहलस्स मुउलेहिं सण्णद्धो तवणीआसोओ। जाव देवीए णिवेदेमि।

———————————————————————————————

(उभे श्रुत्वा प्रहृष्टे।)

 **बकुलावलिका—** आश्वसितु सखी। सत्यप्रतिज्ञा देवी। **(क)**

** मालविका—** तेन हि प्रमदवनपालिकायाः पृष्ठतो भवावः। **(ख)**

** बकुलावलिका—** तथा।

( इति निष्क्रान्ते।)

**इति चतुर्थोऽङ्कः।**

**—————**

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) आससिदु सही। सच्चप्पइरण्णा देवी। (ख) तेण हि पमदवणपालिआए पुठ्ठदो होम। (ग) तह।

———————————————————————————————

**पञ्चमोऽङ्कः।**

**(ततः प्रविशत्युद्यानपालिका।)**

 **उद्यानापालिका—** उपक्षिप्तो मया कृतसत्कारविधेस्तपनीयाशोकस्य वेदिकाबन्धः। यावदनुष्ठितनियोगमात्मानं देव्यै निवेदयामि। (परिक्रम्य) अहो दैवस्यानुकम्पनीया मालविका। तस्यां तथा चण्डी देव्यनेनाशोककुसुमवृत्तान्तेन प्रसादसुमुखी भविष्यति। कुत्र नु खलु भवेत् देवी। (विलोक्य) अहो एष देव्याः परिजनाभ्यन्तरः किमपि जतुमुद्रालाञ्छितां मञ्जूषां गृहीत्वा चतुःशालातः कुब्जः सारसको निष्कामति। प्रक्ष्यामि तावदेनम्। (ततः प्रविशति यथानिर्दिष्टः कुब्जः) **(क)**

** उद्यान॰—** (उपसृत्य) सारसक कुत्र प्रस्थितोसि। **(ख)**

** सारसकः—** मधुकरिके विद्यापारगामिनां ब्राह्मणानां नित्यदक्षिणा दातव्या। तामार्यपुरोहितस्य हस्तं प्रापयितुम्। **(ग)**

** उद्यान॰—** किन्निमित्तम्। **(घ)**

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) उवक्खित्तो मए किदसक्कारविहिणो तवणीआसोअस्स वेदिआबन्धो। जाव अणुठ्ठिदणिओअम् अत्ताणं देवीए णिवेदेमि। तस्सिं तह चण्डिआ देवी इमिणा असोअकुसुमवुत्तन्तेण पसादसुमुही हविस्सदि। कहिं णु खु हवे देवी। अह्मो एसो देवीए परिअणब्भन्तरो किंवि जदुमुद्दालञ्छिदं मञ्जूसं गेणिहअ चदुस्सालादो कुब्जो सारसओ णिक्कमदि। पुच्छिस्स दाव ण। (ख) सारसअ कहिं पत्थिदोसि। (ग) महुअरिए विञ्जापारगामिणं बह्मणाणं णिच्चदक्खिणा दादव्वा। ताम् अज्जपुरोहिदस्स हत्थं पाविदुम्। (घ) किण्णिमित्तम्।

———————————————————————————————

 **सार॰—** यदाप्रभृति श्रुतं सेनापतिना यज्ञतुरङ्गरक्षणे नियुक्तो भर्तृदारको वसुमित्र इति तदाप्रभृति तस्यायुर्निमित्तम् अष्टादशसुवर्णपरिमाणां दक्षिणां देवी दक्षिणीयैः परिग्राहयति। **(क)**

 **उद्यान॰—** युज्यते। अथ कुत्र देवी। किं वानुतिष्ठति। **(ख)**

** सार॰—** मङ्गलगृह आसनस्था भूत्वा विदर्भविषयाद्भ्रात्रा वीरसेनेन प्रेषितं लेखकरैर्वाच्यमानं लेखं शृणोति। **(ग)**

** उद्यान॰—** कः पुनर्विदर्भराजवृत्तान्तः। **(घ)**

** सार॰—** वशीकृतः किल वीरसेनप्रमुखैर्भर्तुर्विजयदण्डैर्विदर्भनाथः। मोचितश्चास्य दायादो माधवसेनः। दूतश्च तेन महासाराणि रत्नवाहनानि शिल्पकारिकाभूयिष्ठं परिजनं चोपायनीकृत्य भर्तुः सकाशं प्रेषितः श्वः किल भर्तारं पश्यतीति। **(ङ)**

** उद्यान॰— **गच्छ। अनुतिष्ठात्मनो नियोगम्। अहमपि देवीं प्रेक्षिष्ये। (इति निष्क्रान्तौ) **(च)**

प्रवेशकः।

(ततः प्रविशति प्रतीहारी।)

 **प्रतीहारी—** आज्ञप्तास्म्यशोकसत्कारव्यापृतया देव्या। विज्ञापय आर्यपुत्रम्। इच्छाम्यार्यपुत्रेण सहाशोकवृक्षस्य प्रसूनलक्ष्मी प्रत्यक्षी-  
\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) जदप्यहुदि सुदं सेणावइणा जण्णातुरङ्गरक्खणे णिउत्तो भट्टिदारओ वसुमित्तोत्ति तदप्पहुदि तस्स आऊसणिमित्तम् अट्ठादससुवण्णपरिमाणं दक्खिणं देवी दक्खिणीएहिं परिग्गाहेदि। (ख) जुज्जइ। अह कहि देवी। किं वा अणुचिठ्ठदि। (ग) मङ्गलघरे आसणत्था भविअ विजब्भविसआदो भादुणा वीरसेणेण पेसिदं लेहकरेहि वाइअमाणं लेहं सुणादि। (घ) को उण विदब्भराअवुत्तन्तो। (ङ) वसीकिदो किल वीरसेणप्पमुहेहि भत्तुणो विजअदण्डेहिं विदब्भणाहो। मोइदो अ से दाआदो माहवसेणो। दूदो अ तेण महासाराणि रअणवाहणाणि सिप्पआरिआभूइठ्ठं परिअणम् अ उवाअणीकरिअ भट्टिणो सआसं पेसिदो सुवो किल भट्टारं देक्खिस्सदित्ति। (च) गच्छ। अणुचिठ्ठ अत्तणो णिओअम्। अह वि देवीं पेक्खिस्सम्।

———————————————————————————————

कर्तुमिति। तद्यावद्धर्मासनगतं देवं प्रतिपालयामि। (इति परिक्रामति) **(क)**

(नेपथ्ये वैतालिकौ)

 **प्रथमः— **दिष्ट्या दण्डेनारिशिरःसु वर्तते देवः।

**परभृतकलव्याहारेषु त्वमात्तरतिर्मधुं  
 नयसि विदिशातीरोद्यानेष्वनङ्ग इवाङ्गवान्।  
विजयकरिणामालानत्वं गतैः प्रबलस्य ते  
 वरद वरदारोधोवृक्षैः सहावनतो रिपुः॥१॥**

** द्वितीयः—**

**विरचितपदं वीरप्रीत्या सुरोपम सूरिभि-  
 श्चरितमुभयोर्मध्येकृत्य स्थितं क्रथकैशिकान्।  
तव हृतवतो दण्डानीकैर्विदर्भपतेः श्रियं  
 परिघगुरुभिर्दोर्भिः शौरेः प्रसह्य च रुक्मिणीम्॥२॥**

 **प्रतीहारी—** एष जयशब्दसूचितप्रस्थानो भर्तेत एवागच्छति। अहमपि तावदस्य प्रमुखात्किञ्चिदपसृत्यैतन्मुखालिन्दतोरणं समाश्रिता भवामि। (इत्येकान्ते स्थिता।) **(ख)**

(ततः प्रविशति सवयस्यो राजा।)

** राजा— **

**कान्तां विचिन्त्य सुलभेतरसम्प्रयोगां  
 श्रुत्वा विदर्भपतिमानमितं बलैश्च।  
धाराभिरातप इवाभिहतं सरोजं  
 दुःखायते च हृदयं सुखमश्नुते च॥३॥**

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) आणत्तह्मि असोअसक्कारवावुदाए देवीए। विण्णावेहि अज्जउत्तम्। इच्छम्हि अज्जउत्तेण सह असोअक्खस्स पसूणलच्छिं पच्चक्खीकादुन्ति। ता जाव धम्मासणगदं देवं पडिवालेभि। (ख) एसो जअसद्दसूइदप्पत्थाणो भट्टा इदो एव्व आअच्छदि। अह वि दाव इमस्स पमुहादो किंवि ओसरिअ एदं मुहालिन्दतोरणं समस्सिदा होमि।

———————————————————————————————

 **विदूषकः—** यथाहं पश्यामि तथैकान्तसुखितो भवान्भविष्यति। **(क)**

 **राजा— **कथमिव।

 **विदूषकः—** अद्य किल देव्या पण्डित कौशिकी भणिता। भगवति यत्त्वं प्रसाधनगर्वं वहसि तद्दर्शय मालविकायाः शरीरे वैदर्भं विवाहनेपथ्यमिति। तया च सविशेषालङ्कृता मालविका। तत्रभवती कदाचित्पूरयेद्भवतोऽपि मनोरथम्। **(ख)**

** राजा—** सखे मदपेक्षानुवृत्त्या निवृत्तेर्ष्याया धारिण्याः पूर्वचरितैः सम्भाव्यते एतत्।

 **प्रतीहारी—** (उपगम्य) जयतु भर्ता। देवी विज्ञापयति। तपनीयाशोकस्य कुसुमसौभाग्यदर्शनेन ममारम्भः सफलः क्रियतामिति। **(ग)**

** राजा—** ननु तत्रैव देवी।

 **प्रतीहारी—** अथ किम्। यथार्हसम्मानसुखितमन्तःपुरं विसृज्य मालविकापुरोगेणात्मनः परिजनेन सह देवं प्रतिपालयति। **(घ)**

** राजा—** (सहर्षं विदूषकं विलोक्य) जयसेने गच्छाग्रतः।

 **प्रतीहारी—** इत इतो देवः। (सर्वे परिक्रामन्ति।) **(ङ)**

** विदूषकः—** (विलोक्य) भो वयस्य किञ्चित्परिवृत्तयौवन इव वसन्तः प्रमदवने लक्ष्यते। **(च)**

** राजा—** यथाह भवान्।  
\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) जह अहं पेक्खामि तह एक्कन्तसुहिदो भवं हविस्सदि। (ख) अज्ज किल देवीए पण्डितकोसिकी भणिदा। भअवदि जं तुम पसाहणगव्वं वहसि त दंसेहि मालविआए सरीरे वैदब्भअं विवाहणेवच्छं ति। ताए अ सविसेसालङ्किदा मालविआ। तत्तहोदी कदावि पूरेइ भवदोवि मणोरहम्। (ग) जेदु भट्टा। देवी विण्णावेदि। तवणीआसोअस्स कुसुमसोहग्गदसणेण मह आरम्भो सफलो करीअदुत्ति। (घ) अह इम्। जहारहसम्भाण सुहिअम् अन्तेउरं विसज्जिअ मालविआपुरोएण अत्तणो परिअणेण सह देवं पडिवालेदि। (ङ) इदो इदो देवो। (च) भो वअस्स किञ्चि परिवुत्तजोव्वणो विअ वसन्तो पमदवणे लक्खीअदि।

———————————————————————————————

**अग्रे विकीर्णकुरबकफलजालकभिद्यमानसहकारम्।  
परिणामाभिमुखमृतोरुत्सुकयति यौवनं चेतः॥४॥**

 **विदूषकः—** (परिक्रम्य) भो अयं स दत्तनेपथ्य इव कुसुमस्तवर्कैस्तपनीयाशोकः। अवलोकयतु भवान्। **(क)**

** राजा— **स्थाने खल्वयं प्रसवमन्थरोऽभूत्। यदिदानीमनन्यसाधारणीं शोभामुद्वहति। पश्य।

**सर्वाशोकतरूणां प्रथमं सूचितवसन्तविभवानाम्।  
निर्वृत्तदोहदेऽस्मिन्सङ्क्रान्तानीव कुसुमानि॥५॥**

 **विदूषकः—** भोः विस्रब्धो भव। अस्मासु सन्निहितेष्वपि धारिणी पार्श्वपरिवर्तिनीं मालविकामनुमन्यते। **(ख)**

** राजा—** (सहर्षम्) सखे पश्य।

**मामियमभ्युत्तिष्ठति देवी विनयादुपस्थिता प्रियया।  
विस्मृतहस्तकमलया नरेन्द्रलक्ष्म्या वसुमतीव॥६॥**

(ततः प्रविशति धारिणी परिव्राजिका मालविका विभवतश्च परिवारः।)

** मालविका—** (आत्मगतम्) जानामि निमित्तं कौतुकालङ्कारस्य। तथापि बिसिनीपत्रगतमिव सलिलं वेपते मे हृदयम्। अपि च दक्षिणेतरदपि मे नयनं बहुशः स्फुरति। **(ग)**

** विदूषकः—** भो वयस्य विवाहनेपथ्येन सविशेषं खलु शोभते अत्रभवती मालविका। **(घ)**

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) भो अअं सो दिण्णणेवच्छो विअ कुसुमत्थवएहिं तवणीआसोओ। ओलोअदु भवम्। (ख) भो विसद्धो होहि। अह्मेसु सण्णिहिदेसु वि धारिणी पासपरिवट्टिणिं मालविअम् अणुमण्णेदि। (ग) जाणामि णिमित्तं कोदुआलङ्कारस्स। तह वि विसिणीपत्तगदं विअ सलिलं वेवदि मे हिअअम्। अविअ दक्खिणेदरं वि मे णअणं बहुसो फुरदि। (घ) भो वअस्स विवाहणेवच्छेण सविसेसं खु सोहदि अत्तहोदि मालविआ।

———————————————————————————————

 **राजा—** पश्याम्येनाम्। यैषा

**अनतिलम्बिदुकूलनिवासिनी बहुभिराभरणैः प्रतिभाति मे।  
उडुगणैरुदयोन्मुखचन्द्रिका गतहिमैरिव चैत्रविभावरी॥७॥**

 **देवी—**(उपेत्य) जयत्वार्यपुत्रः। **(क)**

 **विदूषकः—** वर्धतां भवती। **(ख)**

** परिव्राजिका—** विजयतां देवः।

 **राजा—** भगवति अभिवादये।

 **परिव्राजिका—** अभिप्रेतसिद्धिरस्तु।

 **देवी— (सस्मितम्)** आर्यपुत्र एष तेऽस्माभिस्तरुणीजनसहायस्याशोकः सङ्केतगृहं कल्पितः। **(ग)**

** विदूषकः—** भोः आराधितोऽसि।

 **राजा—** (सव्रीडमशोकमभितः परिक्रामति।) **(घ)**

**नायं देव्या भाजनत्वं न नेयः सत्कारणामीदृशानामशोकः।  
यः सावज्ञो माधवश्रीनियोगे पुष्पैः शंसत्यादरं त्वत्प्रयत्ने॥८॥**

 **विदूषकः—** भो विस्रब्धो भूत्वा त्वं यौवनवतीमिमां पश्य। **(ङ)**

** देवी—** काम्। **(च)**

** विदूषकः—** भवति तपनीयाशोकस्य कुसुमशोभाम्। **(छ)**

(सर्वे उपविशन्ति।)

 **राजा—** (मालविकां विलोक्य आत्मगतम्) कष्टः खलु सन्निधिवियोगः।

**अहं रथाङ्गनामेव प्रिया सहचरीव मे।  
अननुज्ञातसम्पर्का धारिणी रजनीव नौ॥९॥**

( प्रविश्य )

 **कञ्चुकी—** विजयतां देवः। देव अमात्यो विज्ञापयति। तस्मिन्  
\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) जेदु अज्जउत्तो। (ख) वड्डदु भोदी। (ग) अज्जउत्त एस ते अम्हेहिं तणीजणसहाअस्स असोओ सङ्केदघरो कप्पिदो। (घ) भो आराहिओसि। (ङ) भो वीसद्धो भविअ तुमं जोव्वणवदिम् इमं पेक्ख। (च) क। (छ) भोदि तवणीआसोअस्स कुसुमसोहम्।

———————————————————————————————

विदर्भविषयोपायने द्वे शिल्पकारिके मार्गपरिश्रमादलघुशरीरे इति पूर्वं न प्रवेशिते। सम्प्रति देवोपस्थानयोग्ये संवृत्ते। तदाज्ञां देवो दातुमर्हतीति।

 **राजा—** प्रवेशय ते।

** कञ्चुकी—** यदाज्ञापयति देवः। (इति निष्क्रम्य ताभ्यां सह पुनः प्रविश्य) इत इतो भवत्यौ।

 **प्रथमा—** (जनान्तिकम्) सखि मदनिके अपूर्वमिमं राजकुलं प्रविशन्त्याः प्रसीदति मे हृदयम्। **(क)**

** द्वितीया—** ज्योत्स्निके ममापि एवमेव। अस्ति खलु लोकप्रवादः आगामि सुखं दुःखं वा हृदयसमवस्था कथयतीति। **(ख)**

** प्रथमा— **स सत्य इदानीं भवतु। **(ग)**

 **कञ्चुकी—** एष देव्या सह देवस्तिष्ठति। उपसर्पतां भवत्यौ।

(उभे उपसर्पतः।)

(मालविका परिव्राजिका च चेट्यौ दृष्ट्वा परस्परमवलोकयतः।)

 **उभे—** (प्रणिपत्य) जयतु भर्ता। भयतु भट्टिनी। **(घ)**

(राजाज्ञया उभे उपविष्टे।)

 **राजा— **कस्यां कलायामभिविनीते भवत्यौ।

 **राजा—** भर्तः सङ्गीतेऽभ्यन्तरे स्वः। **(ङ)**

** राजा—** देवी गृह्यतामनयोरन्यतरा।

 **देवी—** मालविके इतः पश्य। कतरा ते सङ्गीतसहकारिणी रोचते। **(च)**

** उभे— **(मालविकां दृष्ट्वा) अहो भर्तृदारिका। (प्रणम्य) जयतु जयतु भर्तृदारिका। (इति तया सह बाष्पं विसृजतः।) **(छ)**

(सर्वे सविस्मयमवलोकयन्ति)

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) हला मदणिए अपुव्वम् इमं राअउल पविसन्तीए पसीददि मे हिअअम्। (ख) जोसिणीए महवि एव्वम् एव। अत्थि खु लोअप्पवादो आआमि सुहं दुक्खं वा हिअअसमवत्था कहेदित्ति। (ग) सो सच्चो दाणिं होदु। (घ) जेदु भट्ठा। जेदु भट्ठिणी। (ङ) भट्टा सङ्गीदे अब्भन्तरेह्म। (च) मालविए इदो पेक्ख। कदरा ते सङ्गीदसहआरिणी रुच्चदि। (छ) अह्मो भट्ठिदारिया। जेदु जेदु भट्टिदारिआ।

———————————————————————————————

 **राजा—** के वा भवत्यौ। का वा इयम्

 **उभे—** देव इयमस्माकं भर्तृदारिका। **(क)**

** राजा—** कथमिव।

 **उभे—** शृणोतु भर्ता। यः स भर्त्रा विजयदण्डैर्विदर्भनाथं वशीकृत्य बन्धनान्मोचितः कुमारो माधवसेनो नाम तस्येयं कनीयसी भगिनी मालविका नाम।

 **देवी— **कथं राजदारिकेयम्। चन्दनं खलु मया पादुकोपयोगेन दूषितम्। **(ग)**

** राजा—** अथात्रभवती कथमित्थम्भूता।

 **मालविका—** (निःश्वस्य आत्मगतम्) विधिनियोगेन। **(घ)**

** द्वितीया—** शृणोतु भर्ता। दायादवशङ्गते अस्माकं भर्तृदारके माधवसेने तस्यामात्येन आर्यसुमतिना अस्मादृशं परिजनमुज्झित्वा गूढमपनीतैषा। **(ङ)**

** राजा—** श्रुतपूर्वं मयैतत्। ततस्ततः।

 **द्वितीया—** भर्तः अतः परं न जानीमः। **(च)**

 **परिव्राजिका—** अतः परमहं मन्दभाग्या कथयिष्यामि।

 **उभे— **भर्तृदारिके आर्यकौशिक्या इव स्वरसंयोगः। **(छ)**  
\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) देव इअम् अह्माणं भट्टिदारिआ। (ख) सुणादु भट्टा। जो सो भट्टिणा विजअदण्डेहिं विदब्भणाहं वसीकरिअ बन्धणादो मोइओ कुमारो माहवसेणो णाम तस्स इअं कणीअसी भइणी मालविआ णाम। (ग) कहं राअदारिआ इअम्। चन्दणं खु मए पदुओवओएण दूसिदम्। (घ) विहिणिओएण। (ङ) सुणादु भट्टा। दाआदवसङ्गदे अम्हाणं भट्टिदारए माहवसेणे तस्स अमच्चेण अज्जसुमदिणा अह्मारिसं परिअणम् उज्झिअ गूढम् अवणीदा एसा। (च) भट्टा अदो वरं ण आणीमो। (छ) भट्टिदारिए अज्जकोसिहम्ए विअ सरसञ्जोओ।

———————————————————————————————

 **मालविका—** ननु सैव। **(क)**

** उभे— **यतिवेषधारिण्यार्यकौशिकी दुःखेन विभाव्यते। भगवति वन्दावहे। **(ख)**

** परिव्राजिका—** स्वस्ति भवतीभ्याम्।

 **राजा—** कथमाप्तवर्गोऽयं भगवत्याः।

 **परिव्राजिका—** एवमेतत्।

 **विदू॰—** तेन हि कथयतु भगवत्यत्रभवत्या वृत्तान्तावशेषम्। **(ग)**

** परिव्राजिका—** (सवैक्लव्यम्) श्रूयतां तावत्। माधवसेनसचिवं सुमतिं ममाग्रजमवगच्छ।

 **राजा—** उपलब्धम्। ततस्ततः।

 **परि॰—** स इमां तथागतभ्रातृकां मया सार्धमपवाह्य भवत्सम्बन्धापेक्षया पथिकसार्थं विदिशागामिनमनुप्रविष्टः।

 **राजा— **ततस्ततः।

 **परि॰— **स चाटव्यन्तरे निविष्टो गताध्वा वणिग्जनो विश्रमितुम्।

 **राजा—** ततस्ततः।

 **परिव्राजिका—** ततः

**तूणीरपट्टपरिणद्धभुजान्तराल-  
 माकर्णलम्बिशिखिपिच्छकलापधारि।  
कोदण्डपाणि निनदत्प्रतिरोधकाना-  
 मापातदुष्प्रसहमाविरभूदनीकम्॥१०॥**

(मालविका भयं रूपयति।)

 **विदू॰—** भवति मा बिभेहि। अतिक्रान्तं खलु भगवती कथयति। **(घ)**  
\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) णं सा एव्व। (ख) जदिवेसधारिणी अज्जकोसिई दुक्खेण विभावीअदि। भअवदि वन्दामो। (ग) तेण हि कहेदु भअवदी अत्तहोदीए उत्तन्तावसेसम्। (घ) भोदि मा भआहि। अदिक्कन्तं खु भअवदी कहेदि।

———————————————————————————————

 **राजा—** ततस्ततः।

 **परि॰—** ततो मुहूर्तं बद्धयुद्धास्ते पराङ्मुखीकृताः सार्थवाहयोद्धारस्तस्करैः।

 **राजा—** भगवति अतः परमिदानीं कष्टं श्रोतव्यम्।

 **परिव्राजिका—** ततः स मत्सोदर्यः

**इमां परीप्सुर्दुर्जाते पराभिभवकातराम्।  
भर्तृप्रियः प्रियैर्भर्तुरानृण्यमसुभिर्गतः॥११॥**

 **प्रथमा—** हा हतः सुमतिः। **(क)**

** द्वितीया—** अतः खलु भर्तृदारिकाया इयं समवस्था संवृत्ता। **(ख)**

(परिव्राजिका बाष्पं विसृजति।)

 **राजा— **भगवति तनुभृतामीदृशी लोकयात्रा। न शोच्यस्तत्रभवान्सफलीकृतभर्तृपिण्डः। ततस्ततः।

 **परिव्राजिका—** ततोऽहं मोहमुपगता यावत्सञ्ज्ञामुपलभे तावदियं दुर्लभदर्शना संवृत्ता।

 **राजा—** महत्खलु कृच्छ्रमनुभूतं भगवत्या।

 **परिव्राजिका—** ततो भ्रातुः शरीरमग्निसात्कृत्वा पुनर्नवीभूतवैधव्यदुःखया मया त्वदीयं देशमवतीर्य इमे काषाये गृहीते।

 **राजा—** युक्तः सज्जनस्यैष पन्थाः। ततस्ततः।

 **परिव्राजिका—** तत इयमप्याटविकेभ्यो वीरसेनं वीरसेनाच्च देवीं गता देवीगृहे लब्धप्रवेशया मया पुनर्दृष्टा। इत्येतदवसानं कथायाः।

 **मालविका—** (आत्मगतम्) किं नु खलु साम्प्रतं भर्ता भणति। **(ग)**

** राजा—** अहो परिभवोपहारिणो विनिपाताः। कुतः।

**प्रेष्यभावेन नामेयं देवीशब्दक्षमा सती।  
स्नानीयवस्त्रक्रियया पत्रोर्णं वोपयुज्यते॥१२॥**

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) हा हदो सुमती। (ख) अदो खु भट्ठिदारिआए इअं समवत्था संवुत्ता। (ग) किं णु खु सम्पदं भट्ठा भणादि।

———————————————————————————————

 **देवी—** भगवति त्वयाभिजनवतीं मालविकामनाचक्षाणया असाम्प्रतं कृतम्। **(क)**

** परि॰—** शान्तं पापं शान्तं पापम्। कारणेन खलु मया नैभृत्यमवलम्बितम्।

 **देवी—** किमिव तत्कारणम्। **(ख)**

** राजा—** यदि वक्तव्यं कथ्यताम्।

 **परि॰—** श्रूयताम्। इयं पितरि जीवति केनापि लोकयात्रागतेन सिद्धादेशेन साधुना मत्समक्षमादिष्टा संवत्सरमात्रमियं प्रेष्यभावमनुभूय ततः सदृशभर्तृगामिनी भविष्यतीति। तदवश्यम्भाविनमादेशमस्यास्त्वत्पादशुश्रूषया परिणमन्तमवेक्ष्य कालप्रतीक्षया मया साधु कृतमिति पश्यामि।

 **राजा—** युक्ता प्रतीक्षा।

 **कञ्चुकी—** देव कथान्तरेणान्तरितम्। अमात्यो विज्ञापयति। विदर्भगतमनुष्ठेयमवधारितमस्माभिः। देवस्य तावदभिप्रेतं श्रोतुमिच्छामीति।

 **राजा—** मौद्गल्य तत्रभवतोर्भ्रात्रोर्यज्ञसेनमाधवसेनयोर्द्वैराज्यमिदानीमवस्थापयितुकामोऽस्मि।

**तौ पृथग्वरदाकूले शिष्टामुत्तरदक्षिणे।  
नक्तन्दिवं विभज्योभौ शीतोष्णकिरणाविव॥१३॥**

 **कञ्चुकी—** देव एवममात्यपरिषदे निवेदयामि।

 **राजा—** (अङ्गुल्या अनुमन्यते)

(निष्क्रान्तः कञ्चुकी)

 **प्रथमा—** (जनान्तिकम्) भर्तृदारिके दिष्ट्या भर्तृदारकोऽर्धराज्ये प्रतिष्ठां गमिष्यति। **(ग)**

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) भअवदि तुए अभिजणवदिं मालविअम् अणाचक्खन्तीए असम्पदं किदम्। (ख) किं विअ तं कारणम्। (ग) भट्टदारिए दिट्ठिआ भट्टदारओ अद्धरज्जे पडिठ्ठं गमिस्सदि।

———————————————————————————————

 **मालविका—** एतत्तावद्बहु मन्तव्यं यज्जीवितसंशयान्मुक्तः। **(क)**

(प्रविश्य)

 **कञ्चुकी—** विजयतां देवः। देव अमात्यो विज्ञापयति। कल्याणी देवस्य बुद्धिः। मन्त्रिपरिषदोऽप्येवमेव दर्शनम्। कुतः

**द्विधा विभक्तां श्रियमुद्वहन्तौ धुरं रथाश्वाविव सङ्ग्रहीतुः।  
तौ स्थास्यतस्ते नृपती निदेशे परस्परावग्रहनिर्विकारौ॥१४॥**

 **राजा—** तेन हि मन्त्रिपरिषदं ब्रूहि। सेनापतये वीरसेनाय लिख्यतामेवं क्रियतामिति।

 **कञ्चुकी—** यदाज्ञापयति देवः। (इति निष्कम्य सप्राभृतकं लेखं गृहीत्वा पुनः प्रविष्टः।) अनुष्ठिता प्रभोराज्ञा। अयं पुनरिदानीं देवस्य सेनापतेः पुष्पमित्रस्य सकाशात्सप्राभृतको लेखः प्राप्तः। प्रत्यक्षीकरोत्वेनं देवः।

(राजा सहसोत्थाय सोपचारं गृहीत्वा प्राभृतकं परिजनायार्पयति।)  
(लेखं च नाट्येनोद्वेष्टयति।)

** देवी—** (आत्मगतम्) अहो ततोमुखमेव नो हृदयम्। श्रोष्यामि तावद्गुरुजनस्य कुशलानन्तरं वसुमित्रस्य वृत्तान्तम्। अधिकारे खलु मे पुत्रकः सेनापतिना नियुक्तः। **(ख)**

** राजा—** (उपविश्य नावयति) स्वस्ति। यज्ञशरणात्सेनापतिः पुष्पमित्रो वैदिशस्थं पुत्रमायुष्मन्तमग्निमित्रं स्नेहात्परिष्वज्यानुदर्शयति। विदितमस्तु । योऽसौ राजयज्ञदीक्षितेन मया राजपुत्रशतपरिवृतं वसुमित्रं गोप्तारमादिश्य संवत्सरोपावर्तनीयो निरर्गलस्तुरगो विसृष्टः स सिन्धोर्दक्षिणरोधसि चरन्नश्वानीकेन यवनानां प्रार्थितः। तत उभयोः सेनयोर्महानासीत्सम्मर्दः।  
\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) एदं दाव बहु मन्तव्यं जं जीविदसंसआदो मुत्तो। (ख) अह्महे तदोमुहम् एव्व णो हिअअम्। सुणिस्सं दाव गुरुअणरस कुसलाणन्तरं वसुमित्तस्स वुत्तन्तम्। अहिआरे खु मे पुत्तओ सेनावदिणा णिउत्तो।

———————————————————————————————

(देवी विषादं नाटयति।)

 **राजा— **कथमीदृशं संवृत्तम्। (शेषं पुनर्वाचयति।)

**ततः परान्पराजित्य वसुमित्रेण धन्विना।  
प्रसह्य ह्रियमाणो मे वाजिराजो निवर्तितः॥१५॥**

** देवी—** अनेनाश्वस्तं मे हृदयम्। **(क)**

** राजा—** (लेखशेषं वाचयति) सोऽहमिदानीमंशुमतेव सगरः पौत्रेण प्रत्याहृताश्वो यक्ष्ये। तदिदानीमकालहीनं विगतरोषचेतसा भवता वधूजनेन सह यज्ञसेवनायागन्तव्यमिति।

 **राजा—** अनुगृहीतोऽस्मि।

 **परिव्राजिका—** दिष्ट्या पुत्रविजयेन दम्पती वर्धेते। (देवीं विलोक्य)

**भर्त्रासि वीरपत्नीनां श्लाघ्यानां स्थापिता धुरि।  
वीरसूरिति शब्दोऽयं तनयात्त्वामुपस्थितः॥१६॥**

 **विदू॰—** भवति परितुष्टोस्मि यत्पितरमनुगतो वत्सः। **(ख)**

 **परिव्राजिका—** कलभेन खलु यूथपतिरनुकृतः।

 **कञ्चुकी—** देव अयं कुमारः

**नैतावता वीरविजृम्भितेन  
 चित्तस्य नो विस्मयमादधाति।  
यस्याप्रधृष्यः प्रभवस्त्वमुच्चै-  
 रग्नेरपां दग्धुरिवोरुजन्मा॥१७॥**

 **राजा—** मौद्गल्य यज्ञसेनश्यालमूरीकृत्य मुच्यन्तां सर्वे बन्धनस्थाः।

 **कञ्चुकी—** यदाज्ञापयति देवः। (इति निष्क्रान्तः।)

 **देवी— **जयसेने गच्छ। इरावतीप्रमुखेभ्योऽन्तःपुरेभ्यः पुत्रस्य विजयवृत्तान्तं निवेदय। **(ग)**

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) इमिणा आसंसिदं मे हिअअम्। (ख) भोदि परितुठ्ठोम्हि जं पिदरम् अणुगदो वच्छो। (ग) जयसेणे गच्छ। इरावदिप्पमुहाणम् अन्तेपुराणं पुत्तस्स विअअवुत्तन्तं णिवेदेहि।

———————————————————————————————

 **प्रतीहारी—** तथा। (इति प्रस्थिता)

 **देवी—** एहि तावत्। **(क)**

** प्रतीहारी—** (परिवृत्य) इयमस्मि। **(ख)**

** देवी—** (जनान्तिकम्) यन्मयाशोकदोहदनियोगे मालविकायै प्रतिज्ञातं तदस्या अभिजनं च निवेद्य मम वचनेनेरावतीमनुनय। त्वयाहं सत्यान्न परिभ्रंशयितव्येति। **(ग)**

** प्रती॰—** यद्देव्याज्ञापयति। (इति निष्क्रम्य पुनः प्रविश्य) भट्टिनि पुत्रविजयनिमित्तेन परितोषेणान्तःपुराणामाभरणानां मञ्जूषास्मि संवृत्ता। **(घ)**

** देवी—** किमत्राश्चर्यम्। साधारणः खलु तासां मम चायमभ्युदयः। **(ङ)**

** प्रतीहारी—** (जनान्तिकम्) भट्टिनि इरावती पुनर्विज्ञापयति। सदृशं खलु देव्याः प्रभवन्त्याः वचनं प्रथमसङ्कल्पितं न युज्यतेऽन्यथा कर्तुमिति। **(च)**

** देवी—** भगवति त्वयानुज्ञातेच्छाम्यार्यसुमतिना प्रथमसङ्कल्पितां मालविकामार्यपुत्राय प्रतिपादयितुम्। **(छ)**

** परिव्राजिका—** इदानीमपि त्वमेवास्याः प्रभवसि।  
\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) एहि दाव। (ख) इअं ह्मि। (ग) जं मए असोअदोहलणिओए मालविआए पइण्णादं तं से अहिजणं च णिवेदिअ मह वअणेण इरावदिम् अणुणेहि। तुए अहं सच्चादो ण परिब्भंसइदव्वेत्ति। (घ) जं देवी आणवेदि। भट्टिणि पुत्तविजअणिमित्तेण परितोसेण अन्तेउराणम् आहरणाणं मञ्जूसह्मि संवुत्ता। (ङ) किम् एत्थ अच्चरिरिअम्। साहारणो खु ताणं मह अ अअम् अब्भुदओ। (च) भट्ठिणि इरावदी उण विण्णवेदि। सरिसं क्खु देवीए पहवन्तीए वअणं पुढमसङ्कप्पिदं ण जुज्जदि अण्णहा कादुं ति। (छ) भअवदि तुए अणुण्णादा इच्छामि अज्जसुमदिणा पुढमसङ्कप्पिदं मालविअम् अज्जउत्तस्स पडिवादेदु।

———————————————————————————————

 **देवी— **(मालविकां हस्ते गृहीत्वा) इदमार्यपुत्रः प्रियनिवेदनानुरूपं पारितोषिकं प्रतीच्छतु। (राजा सव्रीडं जोषमास्ते।) **(क)**

** देवी— **(सस्मितम्) किमवधीरयति मामार्यपुत्रः। **(ख)**

 **विदू॰—** भवति एष लोकव्यवहारः सर्वोपि नववरो लज्जातुरो भवति। **(ग)**

(राजा विदूषकमवेक्षते।)

 **विदू॰—** अथवा देव्या प्रणयविशेषं दत्तदेवीशब्दां मालविकामत्रभवान्प्रतिग्रहीतुमिच्छति। **(घ)**

** देवी—** एतस्या राजदारिकाया अभिजनेनैव दत्तो देवीशब्दः। किं पुनरुक्तेन। **(ङ)**

 **परिव्राजिका—** मा मैवम्।

**अप्याकरसमुत्पन्ना मणिजातिरसंस्कृता।  
जातरूपेण कल्याणि न हि संयोगमर्हति॥१८॥**

 **देवी—** (स्मृत्वा) मर्षयतु भगवती। अभ्युदयकथयोचितं मया न लक्षितम्। जयसेने गच्छ तावत्। कौशेयपत्रोर्णमुपनय। **(च)**

** प्रतीहारी—** यद्देव्याज्ञापयति। (इति निष्क्रम्य पत्रोर्णं गृहीत्वा पुनः प्रविश्य) देवि एतत्। **(छ)**

** देवी— **(मालविकामवगुण्ठनवतीं कृत्वा) आर्यपुत्र इदानीमिमां प्रतीच्छतु। **(ज)**  
\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) इदम् अज्जउत्तो पिअणिवेदणाणुरूवं पारितोसिअं पडिच्छदु। (ख) किम् अवधीरेदि मम् अज्जउत्तो ! (ग) भोदि एमो लोअव्यवहारो सव्वो वि णववरो लज्जादुरो होदि। (घ) अह वा देवीए प्पणअविसेसं दिण्णदेवीसद्दं मालविअम् अत्तभवं पडिग्गहीदुम् इच्छदि। (ङ) एदाए राअदारिआए अहिजणेण एव्व दिगणो देवीसद्दो। किं पुणरुत्तेण। (च) मरिसेदु भअवदी। अब्भुदअकहाए उइदं मए ण लक्खिदम्। जअसेणे गच्छ दाव। कोसेअपत्तोण्ण उवणेहि। (छ) जं देवी आणवेदि। देवी एदम्। (ज) अज्जउत्तो दाणिम् इमं परिच्छदु।

———————————————————————————————

 **राजा—** देवि त्वच्छासनादप्रत्युत्तरा वयम्।

 **परि॰—** हन्त प्रतिगृहीता।

 **विदूषकः—** अहो देव्या अत्रभवतोऽनुकूलता। **(क)**

(देवी परिजनमवलोकयति।)

 **परि॰—** (मालविकामुपेत्य) जयतु भट्टिनी। **(ख)**

(देवी परिव्राजिकामवेक्षते।)

** परि॰—** नैतच्चित्रं त्वयि।

**प्रतिपक्षेणापि पतिं सेवन्ते भर्तृवत्सलाः साध्व्ययः।  
अन्यसरितां शतानि हि समुद्रगाः प्रापयन्त्यब्धिम्॥१९॥**

(प्रविश्य)

 **निपुणिका—** जयतु भर्ता। इरावती विज्ञापयति। यदुपचारातिक्रमेण तदा भर्तुरपराद्धं तत्स्वयमेव भर्तुरनुकूलं नाम मयाचरितम्। साम्प्रतं पूर्णमनोरथेन भर्त्रा प्रसादमात्रेण सम्भावयितव्येति। **(ग)**

** देवी—** निपुणिकम् अवश्यं तस्याः सन्देशमनुज्ञास्यत्यार्यपुत्रः। **(घ)**

** निपुणिका—** अनुगृहीतास्मि। **(ङ)**

 **परिव्राजिका—** देवाहममुना भवत्सम्बन्धेन चरितार्थं, माधवसेनं सभाजयितुमिच्छामि यदि मे तव प्रसादः।

 **देवी—** भगवति न युक्तमस्मान्परित्यक्तुम्। **(च)**

** राजा—** भगवति मदीयेषु लेखेषु तत्रभवते त्वामुद्दिश्य सभाजनाक्षराणि पातयिष्यमि।  
\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) अहो देवीए अत्तहोदो अणुऊलदा। (ख) जेदु भट्टिणी। (ग) जेदु भट्टा। इरावदी विण्णावेदि । जम् उवणारादिक्कमेण तदा भट्टिणो अवरद्धं तं सअम् एव्व भत्तुणो अणुऊलं णाम मए आअरिदम्। सम्पदं पुण्णमणोरहेण भत्तुणा पसादमेत्तेण सम्भावइदव्वत्ति। (घ) णिउणिए अवस्सं ताए सन्देसम् अणुजाणिस्सदि अज्जउत्तो। (ङ) अणुगहीदह्मि। (च) भअवदि ण जुत्तम् अह्मो परिच्चइदुम्।

———————————————————————————————

 **परिव्राजिका—** युवयोः स्नेहेन परवानयं जनः।

 **देवी—** आज्ञापयत्वार्यपुत्रः किं भूयोपि प्रियमनुतिष्ठामि। **(क)**

** राजा—** किमतः परमपि प्रियमस्ति। तथापि इदमस्तु।

**त्वं मे प्रसादसुमुखी भव देवि नित्य-  
मेतावदेव हृदये प्रतिपालनीयम्।**

(भरतवाक्यम्)

**आशास्यमीतिविगमप्रभृति प्रजानां  
सम्पद्यते न खलु गोप्तरि नाग्निमित्रे॥२०॥**

(इति निष्कान्ताः सर्वे।)

**इति श्रीकालिदासस्य कृतौ मालविकाग्निमित्रे पञ्चमोऽङ्कः।**

**———————**

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 (क) आणवेदु अज्जउत्तो किं भूओवि पिअम् अणुचिट्ठामि।

———————————————————————————————

**MĀLAVIKĀGNIMITRA**

**ACT I**

**Page 1.**

 May that Lord remove our mental opacities to enable us to have a vision of the right path—the Lord who, though in charge of the sole lordship yielding manifold fruits unto those who bow before him, is himself clad in a tiger's skin; who, though having his body united with that of his beloved, is yet at the head of ascetics whose minds are above the pale of passions; who, though sustaining the whole universe with his eight forms, is still void of all pride. (1)

*\[At the end of the Benediction\]*

 **The Stage-manager— ***\[Looking towards the green-room\] *My worthy friend, just come here.

*\[Entering\]*

 **Actor— **Sir, here am I.

 **The Stage-manager— **I have been asked by the learned audience to produce during the springtide festival the play called Mālavikāgnimitra written by Kālidāsa. So let the music be commenced.

 **Actor—** Prithee, not so. How is it that, ignoring the works of Bhāsa, Kaviputra, Saumallika and others of wide celebrity, the audience is entertaining such a great regard for the composition of this modern poet, Kālidāsa.

 **The Stage-manager— **Ah ! Your statement lacks discernment. See—

 Only because it is old, a thing is not commendable, nor is a poetic composition faulty simply because it is new. The wise, having duly examined, accept the one or the other.

A fool's decision is ever guided by the judgment of others. (2)

 **Actor— **Your honour is an authority.

 **The Stage-manager— **Well, then, make haste.

**Page 2.**

** **I wish to execute the command of the audience, already accepted reverently, just as this attendant of the Queen Dhārinī, smart in service, wishes to execute her command \[Exeunt ambo\] (3)

THE END OF THE PROLOGUE

*\[Enter Bakulāvalikā\]*

 **Bakulāvalikā— **I am commanded by Queen Dhārinī to inquire from the noble Gaṇadāsa, the teacher of dancing, as to how Mālavikā is getting on with the dance called *Chalita *in which instructions have lately been begun. So I am proceeding to the music-hall. \[*Walks about*\]

\[*Enter the second female-servant with an ornament in her hand*\]

** First (female-servant)— **\[*Seeing the other*\] Friend Kaumudikā, whence this daring that, though passing so near, you do not care to cast even a glance this side !

 **Second (female-servant)— **What ! Bakulāvalikā ? Friend, while looking intently and admiringly at the ring of the queen bearing the snake impression, which has been brought by me from the artisan's, I have become an object of your taunt.

 **Bakulāvalikā— **Your gaze is indeed set on the right place. With this ring, from which filaments of rays are shooting forth, the fore-part of your hand appears as if endowed with a flower.

 **Kaumudikā—** Friend, where are you going ?

***Page 3.***

 **Bakulāvalikā— **To enquire at the queen's command from the noble Gaṇadāsa, the teacher of dancing, as to how Mālavikā is faring in her lessons in dancing.

 **Kaumudikā— **Though placed out of the way by such an engagement, she has nevertheless been seen by his lordship.

 **Bakulā.— **Yes. The girl was seen by the side of the queen in a picture.

 **Kaumu.—** How did it happen ?

 **Bakulā— **Listen. The queen, having gone to the painting-hall, stood looking at the picture done by the drawing-master, the colours of which were yet fresh. In the meanwhile arrived the king.

 **Kaumu.—** What next ?

 **Bakulā.— **Then the king, who after the customary greetings had shared the same seat with the queen, seeing in the midst of her attendants Mālavikā very close to her in the picture, asked her ladyship.

 **Kaumu.—** Pray, what?

 **Bakulā.— **“What is the name of this girl**—**a stranger to me**—**drawn in the picture by the side of your ladyship?"

 **Kaumu.— **Extraordinary beauty always attracts attention. What next?

***Page 4.***

*** *****Bakulā.—** Then the king, getting suspicious as his question was unheeded, began to press the queen repeatedly. And as the queen would not reply, the princess Vasulakshmi said, "My brother-in-law, she is Mālavikā."

 **Kaumu.—** This was but natural for a child. Well, go on.

 **Bakulā.—** What else? Now Mālavikā is being scrupulously kept out of the king's sight.

 **Kaumu.— **Friend, attend to your job. I too shall take this ring to the queen. \[*Exit*\]

 **Bakulā.— **\[*Walking about and looking*\] Here comes the noble Gaṇadāsa, the teacher of dancing, out of the music hall. I shall just show myself to him. *\[Walks about\]*

*\[Entering\]*

** Gaṇadāsa—** Admitted that hereditary lore is highly esteemed by all. Ours, however, is no false pride in dancing. For—

 The sages call it a soothing sacrifice of the gods, pleasing to the eyes; Siva divided it two-fold in his own body which is united with that of Umā; in it men's conduct arising from the three qualities (of *Sattva, Rajas and Tamas*) is seen in its various forms. Dancing is generally the sole recreation even for persons of diverse tastes. (4)

 **Page 5**.

 **Bakulā.― ***\[Drawing nigh\]* Sir, I salute you.

 **Gaṇadāsa— **Good girl, may you live long.

 **Bakulā.—** The queen inquires if your pupil Mālavika is not worrying you much in receiving instructions.

 **Gaṇadāsa—** Good girl, inform the queen that she is exceedingly clever and intelligent. Needless to say more.

 In the art of dramatic performance whatever movement expressive of sentiment is taught by me to her, the young girl by improving upon that teaches me in return as it were. (5)

 **Bakulā.—** *\[Aside\]* I see her almost outdoing Irāvati. *(Loudly)* Blessed indeed is your pupil whose tutor is so pleased with her.

 **Gaṇadāsa— **Good girl, as persons of such ability are rare, I ask you whence the queen got this worthy person.

 **Bakulā.—** The queen has a brother of an inferior caste, named Vīrasena. He was put in charge of a frontier fort situated on the banks of the Narmadā river. This girl was sent by him as a present to his sister, considering her fit to be initiated in fine arts.

 **Gaṇadāsa— ***\[Aside\]* In view of her exquisite beauty I deem her to be of no inferior stuff. *\[Aloud\]* Good girl, I am sure of making a name through her. For—

 The art of the teacher, when imparted to an extraordinary pupil, attains greater excellence, even as the water of a cloud, when dropped into the sea-shell, ripens into a pearl. (6)

***Page 6.***

 **Bakulā.—** Well, where is your pupil ?

 **Gaṇadāsa—** After having been instructed in the dance of five modes, she has just now been told to take rest. Having gone to the window overlooking the pond, she is there enjoying the breeze.

 **Bakulā.—** Let your honour now permit me to go, so that by apprising her of your satisfaction with her I may increase her enthusiasm.

 **Gaṇadāsa— **Go and see your friend. I too, being free, shall go home. *\[Exeunt ambo\]*

End of Mishravishkambha.

 \[*Enter the king, with the retinue standing aside, attended by the minister with a letter in his hand.\]*

 **King— **\[*Looking at the minister who had read the letter*\] Vāhatava, what does the king of Vidarbha propose?

** Minister—** Your Majesty, his own destruction.

 **King— **Now let me hear the message.

 **Minister— **This is what he says in reply. "I am commanded by your honour as under, 'your cousin, prince Mādhavasena, who had agreed to a matrimonial connection with me, while coming to me, was on the way attacked and taken prisoner by your frontier guard. Out of regard for me he should be set at liberty by you along with his wife and sister.' Now, surely you are not unaware, as to what is the rule of conduct of kings towards monarchs of equal standing. In this matter, therefore, your honour should take a neutral position. As for his sister, she was lost in the catastrophe following upon the capture. I shall do my best to start a search for her. Now if really your honour is keen on getting Mādhavasena liberated, here are my terms :—

 'If your honour sets free the Maurya minister, my brother-in-law, who is confined, then I too will immediately release Mādhavasena from the prison' (7)

***Page 7.***

 **King— **\[*In rage*\] What ! Does the fool propose to strike a bargain with me ? Vāhatava, the Vidharbha King is my natural foe and adversary. In order to destroy him who is in the hostile camp, let the forces proceed under the command of Vīrasena as already resolved.

 **Minister—** As Your Majesty commands.

 **King—** Or what do you think about it ?

 **Minister—** Your Majesty's observation is indeed in keeping with the political dictum. For**—**

** **An enemy who has only recently been established in his kingdom, is easy to root out because of his not having gained a firm footing among his subjects like a tree which is still unfirm because of its being newly planted. (8)

 **King—** Then true are the words of the writers on politics. Making this as a pretext, let the Commander-in-Chief be asked to mobilise.

 **Minister—** Very well. *\[Exit\]*

*\[The attendants remain standing round the king according to their respective offices\]*

*\[Entering\]*

 **Vidūshaka—** I am ordered by His Majesty, the King, "Gautama, devise a plan whereby Mālavikā, whose picture was accidentally seen by me, may actually come into my view." I too have acted accordingly. Now I shall inform him. *\[Walks about\]*

 **King— **\[*Seeing Vidūshaka*\] Here arrives another minister of mine who is in charge of a different sort of affairs.

 **Vidūshaka— **\[*Approaching*\] May your honour prosper.

 **King—** \[*With a nod*\] Please sit down here.

\[*Vidūshaka sits down*\]

 **King— **Friend, I hope the eye of your intelligence has been busy discovering some method for attaining the desired object.

 **Vidūshaka— **Rather ask about the success of the plan.

 **King— **How?

***Page 8.***

** Vidūshaka— **\[*Whispering*\] In this way.

 **King—** Well done, my friend. It is a clever beginning. Now I feel hopeful in this affair, even though success in it is difficult. For—

 He alone who has a helper is able to obtain the desired object even though beset with obstacles. One, though endowed with eyes, cannot see in darkness the object one looks for without a lamp. (9)

*\[Voice behind the scenes\]*

 Have done with bragging. Only in the presence of the king will it be decided as to which of us is inferior or superior.

 **King—** \[*Having heard*\] Friend, the tree of your clever plan has put forth flowers.

 **Vidūshaka— **Ere long you will see the fruit also.

*\[Enters the Chamberlain\]*

** Chamberlain— **Your Majesty, the minister informs that your Majesty's commands have been carried out. Now Haradatta and Gaṇadāsa, both teachers of dancing as if they were two sentiments in a bodily form, contending with each other for victory seek an interview with Your Majesty. (10)

 **King— **Usher them in.

** Chamberlain― **As Your Majesty commands.

\[*Goes out. Re—enters with them*\]

 This way, sirs, this way.

 **Haradatta—** \[*Looking at the King*\] Oh, how difficult of approach is the majesty of the king! For—

 Not that he is not known, nor is it that he is inaccessible, and yet it is with awe that I draw near his side. Like the ocean, he, though the same, appears to my eyes new every moment.(11)

 **Gaṇadāsa—** Grand indeed is this splendour in a human form ! Look—

***Page 9.***

 Even though allowed to enter by the guards at the gate and approaching the king with the attendant privileged to move about the throne, I am held back, as it were, even without words, by his lustre which dazzles my eyes.(12)

 **Chamberlain—** Here is His Majesty. Advance, sirs.

** Both—** Victory to Your Majesty.

 **King— **Welcome to both of you. \[*Looking at the attendants*\] Fetch seats for these two gentlemen.

*\[Both sit down on the seats brought by the attendants\]*

 **King— **What brings the two teachers here simultaneously when they should be teaching their pupils?

 **Gaṇadāsa—** May Your Majesty hear. I learnt the science of dramatical acting from a worthy teacher. I have also given exhibitions of the same. I have been patronized by Your Majesty as well as by the Queen.

 **King—** I know it very well. What then?

 **Gaṇadāsa— **I have been insulted in the presence of important persons by this Haradatta, saying "This fellow is not equal even to the dust of my feet."

 **Haradaṭṭa― **Your Majesty, it was he who first indulged in slander against me, remarking, "Between this honourable gentleman and myself there is but the same difference as is between a pond and a sea." Let Your Majesty therefore test me and this person, both in the theory as well as the practical application of our art. Your Majesty who is a connoisseur, will be our judge.

 **Vidūshaka— **Well proposed.

 **Gaṇadāsa— **A first–rate suggestion. Your Majesty may be pleased to hear us attentively.

 **King— **Wait a moment. In this matter the queen might suspect partiality. Therefore let this dispute be decided in her presence and that of the learned Kauśikī.

 **Vidūshaka— **Your honour has observed aright.

***Page 10.***

 **Both teachers— **As it pleases Your Majesty.

 **King— **Maudgalya, having communicated this matter to the queen and the learned Kauśikī, call them here.

 **Chamberlain— **As Your Majesty commands.

\[*Goes out, re-enters with the Queen and the Parivrājikā*\]

 This way, Your ladyship, this way.

 **Queen—** \[*Looking at Parivrājikā*\] Revered lady, what is your view about this contest between Haradaṭṭa and Gaṇadāsa?

 **Parivrājikā—** Have no fears of the defeat of your side. Gaṇadása is not inferior to his rival.

 **Queen— **Nevertheless, the patronage of the King lends superiority to him (Haradaṭṭa)

 **Parivrājikā—** But Your ladyship should also consider the fact that you too bear the title of 'Queen';

 The fire attains excessive lustre by the favour of the sun. But the moon too when favoured by the night acquires great brilliance.(13)

 **Vidūshaka— **Hush, hush! Here arrives the queen Dhāriṇī preceded by her parasite, the learned Kauśikī.

 **King—** I see her—

 Who, adorned with auspicious ornaments and in the company of Kauśikī robed as an ascetic looks like the knowledge of the three Vedas incarnate, accompanied by the knowledge of the individual soul. (14)

 **Parivrājikā― **\[*Approaching*\] May Your Majesty be victorious.

 **King— **Revered lady, I salute you.

***Page 11**.*

 **Parivrājikā— **May you be for a hundred years lord of Dhāriṇī, the queen, and the earth both of whom are alike in forbearance and are producers of excellent things. (15)

 **Dhāriṇī—** May my lord be victorious.

 **King—** Welcome to your ladyship. \[*Looking at Parivrājikā*\] Revered lady, please take your seat.

\[*All sit down in their proper places.*\]

 **King—** Revered lady, there has arisen a dispute as to their respective knowledge between these two gentlemen, Haradatta and Gaṇadāsa. So in this matter your revered ladyship should occupy the position of the judge.

 **Parivrājikā— **\[*With a smile*\] Enough of this joke. Is the jewel to be tested in a village, when the town is close by?

 **King—** Nay, not so. The learned Kauśikī is indeed a saint. The queen and I are however partisans of these two.

 **Teachers—** Your majesty has observed aright. The revered lady, occupying the position of a neutral will be quite competent to distinguish between our respective merits and demerits.

 **King― **Then let the contest commence.

 **Parivrājikā―**Your Majesty, practical demonstration is the main thing in the dramatic art. Why indulge in wordy discussions? Or, what does the queen think?

 **Queen—** If you invite my opinion, I do not at all like this dispute between these two.

 **Gaṇadāsa— **Your ladyship should not imagine that I am likely to be defeated by one who is my peer in learning.

 **Vidūshaka—** Your ladyship, let us enjoy a fight between these two rams. Why give them salaries for nothing?

 **Queen— **You are indeed fond of quarrels.

***Page 12.***

 **Vidūshaka— **Not so. When two excited elephants are fighting with each other, whence can there be any peace unless one of them is vanquished ?

 **King— **Surely your ladyship has seen the graceful acting of these two.

 **Parivrājikā― **Yes.

 **King—** Then what else should they now show to convince us?

 **Parivrājikā— **That is what I was about to say.

 Of one acting is commendable when it is performed by oneself; of another, teaching is remarkable. He, of whom both are excellent, deserves to be placed at the head of teachers. (16)

 **Vidūshaka— **Sirs, have you heard the words of the revered lady? The meaning in a nutshell is that a decision will be made after examining your teaching.

 **Haradatta— **I wholly agree to it.

 **Gaṇadāsa— **Your ladyship, it is decided.

 **Queen— **But if a dull–witted pupil spoils the instruction of her teacher, is the latter to blame?

 **King—** Your ladyship, it is exactly so. The very acceptance of incompetent stuff shows the inferiority of the teacher's judgment.

 **Queen—** *\[Aside\]* What to do now? I don't like the fulfilment of my lord's desire, which would only encourage him. *\[Looking at Gaṇadása\]*. Desist from this meaningless enterprise.

 **Vidūshaka— **Right is the suggestion of your ladyship. My dear Gaṇadása, why should you have anything to do with a contest in which you will be easily defeated, when you are enjoying the sweets offered to Sarasvati under the pretext of teaching music?

***Page 13.***

 **Gaṇadāsa— **True, only this can be the meaning of the queen's words. Listen, this is what suits the occasion―

 One who is afraid of a contest for the simple reason that he has received an office, who suffers disgrace at the hands of others and whose learning is merely for the sake of livelihood—him they call a trafficker dealing in the wares of knowledge. (17)

 ** Queen— **Your pupil has only been recently made over to you. Hence it is not advisable to exhibit the instruction not yet fully matured.

 **Gaṇadása—** That is exactly why I insist.

 **Queen—** Then let both of you show your teaching to the revered lady alone.

 **Parivrajikā― **Your ladyship this is not fair. The decision given by a single person, however learned, is open to criticism.

 **Queen— **\[*Aside*\] Fool, why do you take me to be asleep when I am wide awake?

*\[Turns away in anger\]*

*\[The king shows the queen to Parivrajikā\]*

 **Parivrajikā― **O moon–faced lady, why do you turn away your face from His Majesty without a reason? For, housewives, even though wielding immense power over their lords get angry with them only for some cause. (18).

 **Vidūshaka—** Indeed her anger is not without a cause. She must protect her own man. *\[Looking at Gaṇadása\]* Fortunately you have been saved by her ladyship under the pretence of anger. Every one, though well–trained is not necessarily an adept in displaying one's instruction.

***Page 14.***

 **Gaṇadāsa— **Listen, your ladyship. See how people take it. Now, if you don't permit me who is desirous of exhibiting his power of imparting instruction in this contest, I shall consider myself to be abandoned by you. (19).

*\[Wants to rise up from his seat.\]*

 **Queen—** \[*Aside*\] What help ? \[*Aloud*\] The teacher has full power over his pupils.

 **Gaṇadāsa—** My fears were quite out of place all along. \[*Looking at the king*\] I am permitted by the queen. Let Your Majesty therefore command in what special subject of acting I should exhibit my teaching.

 **King—** As the revered lady commands.

 **Parivrajikā― **The queen has something in her mind. Hence I am afraid to speak out.

 **Queen— **Speak out fearlessly. Surely I would still have control over my own attendants.

 **King— **Say over me too.

 **Queen— **Revered lady speak out now.

 **Parivrajikā—** Your Majesty, they say the *chalita* dance, consisting of four parts, is difficult to perform. Therefore we should witness the practical demonstration of this very dance by these two gentlemen. That alone will suffice to show the inferiority and superiority of their teaching.

** Both teachers— **As the revered lady commands.

 **Vidūshaka—** Then let both the the parties, having made arrangements for music in the audience–hall send a messenger to us. Or, rather the sound of the drum will rouse us.

 **Haradatta— **Very well. \[*Rises up*\]

\[*Gaṇadāsa looks at Dhārīṇī*\]

** Queen—** \[*Looking at Gaṇadāsa*\] May you be victorious. Surely I am not opposed to your victory.

*\[Both the teachers depart\]*

***Page 15.***

 **Parivrājikā― **Just come here.

 **Both teachers— **\[*Turning round*\] Here we are.

 **Parivrājikā― **I am speaking in the capacity of a judge. Let both the pupils enter sparsely clad, so that the grace of all the parts of her body may be well displayed.

** Both—** We need no instructions on this point. \[*Exeunt ambo*\].

 **Queen—** \[*Looking at the King*\] How splendid it would be if my lord were to possess the same resourcefulness in state-affairs also !

 **King—** Do not take it otherwise. O high-minded lady, this has not been at all manoeuvred by me. Generally persons of equal talents get jealous of one another's reputation. (20).

\[*Behind the scenes the sound of the drum. All lend their ears to it.*\]

 **Parivrājikā— **Ah! The music has commenced. For, this Resonant sound of the drum, rising from the middle tune, delightful to the peacocks who respond to it with upraised necks, as they suspect it to be the thunder of rain-clouds, enraptures the mind. (21).

 **King—** Your ladyship, let us join the audience.

 **Queen—** \[*To herself*\] Oh the impudence of my lord !

\[*All rise up*\]

 **Vidūshaka—** \[*Aside to the king*\] Please go slowly, lest her ladyship, Dhārinī, should thwart the plan.

 **King—** The musical sound of the tabor hastens me in spite of my endeavour to maintain fortitude, as if it were the sound of my desire hurrying down the path of fulfilment. (22)

*\[Exeunt Omnes\]*

END OF ACT I

**ACT II**

***Page 16.***

 \[*When all concert arrangements have been made, enter the king, seated, with his friend, Dhārinī, Parivrājikā. and retinue in order of rank.*\]

 **King— **Revered lady, of the two respected teachers whose teaching shall we see first ?

 **Parivrājikā— **Although their proficiency in the art is equal, surely Gaṇadāsa deserves precedence for his age.

 **King— **Maudgalya, go, attend to your duty and inform the two gentlemen about it.

 **Chamberlain— **As Your Majesty commands. \[*Exit*\]

\[*Entering*\]

 **Gaṇadāsa— **Your Majesty, there is a composition of Sharmiśthā attuned to the middle time, consisting of four feet. Your Majesty may be pleased to hear all attentively the recital of one-fourth part of it.

 **King—** Owing to my great esteem for the teacher I am all attention.

\[*Exit Gaṇadāsa*.\]

 **King—**\[*A side*\] Friend,

 My eye, eager to have a look at her who is inside the green-room, is through impatience intent, as it were, on drawing aside the curtain. (1)

 **Vidūshaka—** \[*Aside*\] Well, the honey for the eye is there—but the bee is also close by. Look, therefore, with due caution.

\[*Enter Mālavikā with her teacher carefully studying the grace of her limbs.*\]

 **Vidūshaka— ***\[Aside to the king\]* Behold, Sir. In no way does her loveliness fall short of her picture.

***Page 17.***

 **King—** \[*Aside to Vidūshaka*\] Friend, When I saw her in the picture, my mind feared lest she should not be so beautiful—but now methinks that he who painted her was lacking in attention. (2)

 **Gaṇadāsa― **My child, don't be nervous, keep composed.

 **King― **\[*Aside*\] Oh ! What a beauty flawless in every limb ! Look―

 Her face has long eyes and is as bright as the moon in autumn: her arms are drooping at the shoulders; her bosom is compact with its close and swelling breasts; her sides are polished, as it were; her waist may be measured with the hand; her hips are broad; her feet have curved toes―(in short), her body appears to have been fashioned according to the ideal in the mind of the teachers. (3)

 **Mālavikā— **\[*Having sung the preliminary song sings a quatrain.*\]

 My love is beyond reach. O heart, give up all hope of him. Oh ! the outer corner of my left eye throbs violently. Here I see him after a long time. How should he be drawn near ? Believe me, my lord, dependant though I am, I yearn for you ever so much. (4)

\[*Then she represents dramatically the sentiments of the song*.\]

 **Vidūshaka—** Through the medium of this quatrain her ladyship has as if surrendered herself to you.

 **King―** \[*Aside to Vidūshaka*\] Friend, this is my view also.

 As she dramatically represented the words of the song, "believe me, my lord, to be fondly attached to you," pointing to her person, I myself was, as it were, addressed under the plea of this subtle appeal. For, she saw no other way of expressing her love owing to the presence of Dhāriṇī. (5)

\[*At the end of the song Mālavikā wants to go*\]

***Page 18***

 **Vidūshaka― **Madam, stop a while. You have omitted a particular step. I shall presently question you about it.

 **Gaṇadāsa—** Stay, my child. You will leave after you have proved your instruction to be faultless.

*\[Mālavikā turns back and stands\]*

 **King—** \[*Aside*\] Oh, in all postures her grace adds to her beauty ! Look—

 Having placed on the hip her left hand with the bracelet montionless on the wrist, letting the other hang loose like the bough of the Shyāmā creeper, casting her eyes on the floor on which the flowers are being gently stirred by the toes. She keeps the upper half of the body straight and drawn up thus—her standing posture is more graceful than her dance.

 **Queen—** Does your honour take Gautama's words seriously?

 **Gaṇadāsa— **Nay, your ladyship, not so. Owing to his association with His Majesty it is quite possible that Gautama may be keen-sighted.

 Even a dance becomes sharp–witted by association with the wise, just as turbid water becomes clear by contact with the mud-destroying fruit. (7)

 \[*Looking at Vidūshaka*\] Than let us hear what your honour has to say.

 **Vidūshaka—** \[*Looking at Gaṇadása*\] Ask the judge first. Afterwards I shall point out the omission of the special step noticed by me.

 **Gaṇadása—** Revered lady, speak out according to your observation—it may be a merit or a demerit.

 **Parivrājikā― **According to what I have seen, every thing is faultless. For**—**

 The import was well expressed by her limbs pregnant with words; the step was in tune with the time: there was complete identification with the sentiments: the acting proceeding from her limbs was simply graceful; in the continuance of the successive stages of the acting one sentiment drove out another according to the contest, but the musical interest was maintained. (8)

***Page 19.***

 **Gaṇadāsa— **Or, what does His Majesty think ?

 ** King— **Gaṇadāsa, my pride for my side is shaken.

 **Gaṇadāsa— **To–day am I a dancing master.

 The teaching of a teacher, which does not tarnish before the learned like gold in fire—that alone the wise reckon as faultless. (9)

 **Queen—** I congratulate you, sir, on your giving full satisfaction to the judge.

 **Gaṇadāsa— **The queen's patronage alone is the cause of my success.

 \[*Looking at Vidūshaka*\] Gautama, now speak out what is in your mind.

 **Vidūshaka—** At the first exhibition of a teacher's instruction a Brahman should first be worshipped. That you have forgotten altogether.

 **Parivrājikā—** Oh, what a connoisseur of the dramatic performance is the questioner !

*\[All laugh. Mālavikā too Smiles\]*

 ** King—** \[*A side*\] My eye has enjoyed the quintessence of its function, since it

 Has seen the smiling face of the lady with the large eyes beaming with the radiance of the partially exposed teeth, the face which thus resembles an opening lotus, the filaments of which are not fully visible. (10)

 **Gaṇadāsa—** Great Brahmana ! Surely this is not the first musical concert on the stage. Otherwise, how could we have omitted to worship you who deserves to be worshipped ?

 **Vidūshaka— **Like a foolish Chātaka I indeed looked for water in the sky roaring with dark clouds.

 **Parivrājikā—** Quite so.

***Page 20***

 **Vidūshaka— **Well then, the fools must be guided by the satisfaction of the learned. Since your ladyship has approved (of her performance,) I shall give her this present.

*\[Saying so, he pulls off a bracelet from the king's hand.\]*

 **Queen— **Just wait. Without comparing the merits, why do you give away this ornament ?

 **Vidūshaka— **Because it belongs to another.

 **Queen— ***\[Looking at the teacher\]* Noble Gaṇadasa, I suppose your pupil has exhibited her training.

 **Gaṇadāsa—** Come, my child, let us go now.

*\[Exit Mālavikā with the teacher.\]*

 **Vidūshaka—** *\[Looking at the king, aside to him\]* Only so far could my wit go to serve your honour.

 ** King—** *\[Aside to Vidūshaka\]* No, don't you put a limit to it. For, now I consider her disappearance as the setting of the good star of my eyes, as the end of the great festival of my heart, as the shutting of the door upon my fortitude. (11)

 **Vidūshaka— ***\[Aside to the king.\]* Well, like a poor patient you want the doctor himself to get you the medicine.

 ***Page 21.***

*\[Entering\]*

 **Haradatta—** Your Majesty, you may be pleased to witness my performance now.

 **King—** *\[Aside\]* Gone is the motive of seeing (the performance) \[Resorting to courtesy, aloud\] Haradatta, we are indeed very eager (to see it).

 **Haradatta—** I am so obliged.

*\[Voice behind the scenes\]*

 **A bard— **Victory, victory to Your Majesty !

 It is the noon-tide now. Look—

 The swans are resting with closed eyes under the shade of the leaves of the lotus plants in the lakes; on the places the pigeons are loth, to touch the sloping roofs; the peacock, desirous of drinking the tossed–up water drops, flies round the revolving fountain; and the sun shines with all his rays, as you shine with all your kingly qualities. (12)

 **Vidūshaka—** Ho ! Ho ! The Brahmana's dinner–time has arrived; Your Majesty's also. The violation of the regular hours is condemned by the doctors. Haradatta, what do you say now ?

 **Haradatta―**There is no room for me to say anything in the matter.

 **King— ***\[Looking at Haradatta.\]* Well then, we shall see your performance tomorrow. You may please take rest.

 **Haradatta—** As Your Majesty commands. \[*Exit*\]

 **Queen—** My Lord, take your bath.

***Page 22.***

 **Vidūshaka—** Madam, see to it that the dinner is served quickly.

 **Parivrajikā—** \[*Rising up*\] Farewell to your honour. *\[Exit* *with the queen and her attendants\]*

 **Vidūshaka— **Oh ! Mālavikā is peerless not only in her beauty but also in her art.

 **King— **Friend,

 The Creator, when he endowed that artless beauty with fine talents, fashioned indeed a poisoned arrow for Cupid. (13)

 What more? You should anxiously think of me.

 **Vidūshaka— **And you of me. The pit of my stomach is awfully burning like an oven in the market.

 **King—** In the same way expedite matters for the sake of your friend.

 **Vidūshaka—** Yes, if an opportunity offers itself. But, like moonlight screened by clouds, a sight of her ladyship is dependent on others. Your honour too, like a bird hovering over a slaughter–house, hankers after the meat and is yet timid. Therefore, I should like to see you seeking the attainment of your object without being impatient.

 **King— **Friend, how can I help being impatient?

 That beautiful-eyed lady has become the sole centre of love for me whose heart is now withdrawn from all affairs with the ladies of the harem. (14)

*\[Exeunt Omnes\]*

***Page 23.***

**ACT III **

*\[Enters a female attendant of the Parivrajiká\]*

 **The female attendant— **I have been ordered by the revered lady, 'Samábhrtikā, fetch me a citron for presenting to the queen. I shall therefore look for Madhukarikā, the keeper of the pleasure-garden. \[Walking about and seeing\] Here stands Madhukarikā looking at the golden Asoka.I shall approach her.

*\[Enter the keeper of the garden.\]*

 **First— ***\[Approaching\]* Madhukarikā, are you getting on well with your work in the garden?

 **Second— **Oh, Samābhrtikā, ! Friend, welcome to you.

 **Samābhrtikā― **Friend, her ladyship commands, "Her Majesty, the queen, should not be seen by persons like us emptyhanded. Therefore I wish to wait on her with a citron.

 **Madhukarikā— **The citron is quite close at hand. But tell me first which of the two contesting teachers of dancing did the revered lady praise after having seen their teaching.

 ** Samābhrtikā—** Both indeed are versed in theory and equally proficient in practical demonstration. But owing to the uncommon excellence of his pupil Gaṇādāsa ranked the higher.

 **Madhukarikā— **But what is all this scandal that we hear about Mālavikā ?

***Page 24.***

 **Samā—** His lordship is furiously in love with her. But out of his regard for the feelings of queen Dhāriṇī he does not assert himself. Mālavikā also in these days appears to be withering like a jasmine garland thrown away after use. More than this I do not know. Allow me to go now.

 ** Madhu.—** But take the citron hanging on this branch.

 ** Samā.—** *\[Gesticulates taking the citron\]* Friend, you will also get a fruit far better than this—for this service to a saintly person.

 ** Madhu— **Friend, we shall go together. I have also to inform the queen about the longing of the golden Aśoka which is delaying to put forth flowers.

 ** Samā.—** Right: This indeed is your duty.

*\[Exeunt ambo\]*

*\[End of the interlude.\]*

* \[Enter the king in a love-born state and Vidūshaka.\]*

 **King— ***\[Looking at himself\]*

 The body may grow thin, as it misses the pleasure of the beloved's embrace. The eye may be tearful, since she is not seen even for a moment. But, O heart, you are never away from that fawn-eyed lady. Why do you then suffer anguish when uninterrupted bliss is your privilege? (1)

***Page 25.***

 **Vidūshaka— **Have done with your cowardly lamentations. I saw Bakulāvalikā. The dear friend of her ladyship Mālavikā, and I conveyed to her your honour's message.

 **King—** Then what did she say?

 **Vidūshaka— **Inform his lordship. 'I am favoured by this mission. But that poor girl is not easily accessible ass shei guarded by Her Majesty more closely than ever like a treasure guarded by a serpent. Still I shall manage somehow.'

 **King―** O mighty Cupid, having directed my heart to objects beset with impediments, why do you smite me in a way that I am unable to brook any delay. \[*Wonderingly*\]

 Where on the one hand is the tormenting heart-ache and where on the other is your innocent-looking weapon ! What they call soft and yet very sharp, is, O Cupid, seen in you. (2)

 **Vidūshaka— **I tell you that I have already made a beginning towards the attainment of the desired object. Therefore, your honour may compose yourself.

 **King—** Well, where shall I pass the rest of the day when my mind is averse to normal duties ?

 **Vidūshaka— **This very day Irāvati has sent you a present of the red Kurābaka flowers suggestive of the first dawn of spring and, making the recent advent of spring an excuse, has requested your honour through Nipunikā, 'I wish to enjoy a spell of swinging with you.' Your honour also promised this to her. So let us go to the pleasure-garden.

***Page 26.***

 **King—** This is not expedient.

 **Vidūshaka— **Why?

 **King— **Friend, women are naturally shrewd. How will your friend fail to notice that my affections are transferred to another, even though I would be caressing her? Hence I conclude―

 'Tis better to turn down her request though reasonable, for I can find many excuses for rejecting it. But certainly it is not advisable to pay attentions to high-minded ladies, even though more assiduous than before, if they are void of affection. (3)

 **Vidūshaka— **It does not become your honour to do away at one stroke with your usual courtesy towards the ladies of the harem.

** King—** *\[Reflecting\]* Then lead me to the pleasure-garden.

 **Vidūshaka— **This way, your honour, this way.

*\[Both walk about\]*

 **Vidūshaka—** By means of its leafy fingers shaken by the wind, the spring indeed seems to hasten your honour to enter the pleasure garden.

 **King— ***\[Gesticulating the pleasure of touch\]* The spring, no doubt, is courteous, Friend, see—"The Spring, sympathetically enquiring, as it were about the bearableness of love's agony through the dulcet notes of the excited cuckoos, has blown across my body the soothing breeze of the South laden with the fragrance of the mango-blossoms, as if it were the soft palm of his hand. (4)

 **Vidūshaka—** Enter so that you may get relief.

*\[Both enter\]*

***Page 27.***

 **Vidūshaka― **O friend, just mark carefully. How the Vernal Beauty, as if to allure your honour, has put on a dress of spring flowers which puts to shame the apparel of a young lady.

 **King—** Really I am surprised to see it.

 The red paint of the Bimba-like lower lip is excelled in its hue by the lustre of the flaming Aśoka flower; the painting on the face is put to shame by the dark-blue, white and red Kurabaka flower; the forehead is surpassed by the Tilaka flower to which the bees are clinging like collyrium. The Vernal Beauty is as if disdainful of the young ladies in the art of decoration of the face. (5)

*\[Both look intently at the beauty of the garden\]*

*\[Enter love-lorn Mālavikā\]*

 **Malā—** Longing for the king whose heart is unknown, I feel ashamed even of myself. Whence shall I muster courage to speak this matter even to my dear friends. I know not how long Cupid will afflict me with this pain, unbearable for want of a remedy. *\[Walking a few steps\]* Where am I going to? *\[Reflecting\]* Oh, I see, I have been directed by the queen,"Owing to a fall from the swing because of Gautama's rashness, my feet are paining. Do you therefore go and satisfy the craving of the golden Aśoka. If it puts forth flowers within five nights time, I *\[breaking off with a sigh\]* shall give you a reward that would fulfil your desire. I shall therefore first go to the place where I have to carry out this command. While Bakulāvalikā follows me with the foot ornaments in her hand, I shall for a moment freely give vent to my grief. \[*Walks about*\]

***Page 28*.**

 **Vidūshaka— **\[*Seeing*\] Ho ! Ho ! Here indeed is sugar available for one who is cloyed with liquor.

 **King—** Eh, what is that ?

 **Vidūshaka— **Here is Mālavikā, not very far, all alone, sparsely clad and full of longing.

 **King—** *\[Joyfully\]* What ! Mālavikā?

 **Vidūshaka— **Yes.

 **King— **'Tis possible now to sustain life.

 On hearing from you that my beloved is near, my depressed heart has cheered up, as does the heart of a thirsty traveller on knowing from the cry of a crane that some tree-hid stream is at hand. (6)

 But where is her ladyship?

 **Vidūshaka— **Here is she seen emerging from the heart of the grove and coming in this very direction.

***Page 29.***

 **King— ***\[Seeing joyfully\]* Friend I see her.

 Broad at the round lips, slim at the waist, swelling at the breasts, and very large in the eyes,—here comes she, my very life. (7)

 Friend, now her ladyship is in a different state, far more charming than before. Look—with cheeks pale like a reed and with a few ornaments, she looks like a jasmine creeper with leaves ripened by spring and with a few flowers.

 **Vidūshaka— **Like your honour she also seems to be affected by the malady of love.

 **King— **'Tis friendship that sees so.

 **Mālavikā― **There is that Aśoka, which longing for a pleasing kick and being without its garment of flowers resembles me who is full of longing. I shall just sit down on this cool slab under the shade and divert myself.

 **Vidūshaka—** Has your honour heard ? "Full of longing" that is what her ladyship says.

 **King—** From this alone I cannot give you credit for lucid reasoning. For—

 Wafting the pollen of the Kurabaka flowers and surcharged with the spray from the opening of tender leaves the Malaya breeze produces a longing in the mind even without a cause. (9)

*\[Mālavikā sits down\]*

 **King—** Friend, come here. Let us conceal ourselves behind the creeper.

 **Vidūshaka— **I imagine Irāvati is not far off.

 **King— **Seeing the lotus-pool, the elephant does not mind the alligator. *\[Keeps on Looking.\]*

***Page 30.***

 **Mālavikā—** O heart, have done with this desire which is without a prop and has stepped beyond all limits. Why do you torment me?

\[Vidūshaka significantly looks at the king\]

 **King—** My sweet-heart, see the perversity of love.

 You do not disclose the cause of your longing, nor does guess hit upon the exact truth. Yet, O fair lady, I consider myself to be the object of these lamentations. (10)

 **Vidūshaka— **Your honour's doubts will presently be removed. Here is Bakulāvalikā, who was entrusted with your love-message, coming to her in private.

 **King— **I hope she remembers my request.

 **Vidūshaka— **What ! Can this jade forget your important message? Even I remember it all right.

*\[Entering with the foot ornaments in her hand\]*

 **Bakulāvalikā— **Friend, are you doing well ?

 **Mālavikā― **Oh, Bakulāvalikā ! Friend, welcome, to you. Sit down.

 **Bakulāvalikā— **\[*Sitting down*\] Friend, on this occasion you are entrusted with the duty, as you are fit for it. Therefore give me one of your feet so that I may adorn it with the lac paint and an anklet.

***Page 13.***

 **Mālavikā―** O heart, don't exult that this exalted position has come your way. How can I escape now ? Or rather this itself will be my funeral decoration.

 **Bakulāvalikā― **What are you thinking? The queen, as you are aware, is anxious about the blossoming of this golden Aśoka.

 **King― **What, is all this affair meant for gratifying the longing of the Aṣoka?

 **Vidūshaka― **Have you indeed been thinking**―**" it is for me that the queen has caused her to be adorned with the finery of the harem"?

 **Mālavikā― **Friend, pray excuse me for this \[*She offers her foot*.\]

 **Bakulāvalikā— **Why, you are my own self. \[*She begins painting the foot*\].

 **King― **Friend, see the fresh line of colour drawn along the edge of the foot of my beloved. It looks like the fresh sprouting of the tree of Cupid burnt down by Śiva."

 ** Vidūshaka—** A duty fitting indeed for her foot has been assigned to her ladyship.

 ** King—** You have observed aright.

 With the fore-part of her foot red as the new sprout and diffusing radiance from its nails, this young lady may well strike the two―the unblossomed Aśoka waiting for the fulfilment of its longing, and her lover who has bowed down his head for a recent offence." (12)

 **Vidūshaka— **Her ladyship will certainly strike you when you have committed an offence.

***Page 32*.**

 ** King—** I accept the words of the prophetic Brāhmana.

*\[Enter Irāvati in a state of intoxication, and hermaid-servant.\]*

 **Irāvati—** Nipuṇikā, my girl, I have often heard that drunkenness lends a peculiar charm to women. Is this saying true ?

 ** Nipuṇikā—** Hitherto it was a mere saying, To day, however, it has proved to be a fact.

 **Irāvati—** Have done with compliments. Tell me whence you came to know that his lordship had gone to the swinghouse first.

 **Nipuṇikā― **From his unfaltering affection for you.

 **Irāvati— **Away with flattery, speak as a neutral.

 ** Nipu.— **I was told so by the noble Gautama who is always greedy of the spring presents. Let my lady hurry up.

 **Ira.— **\[*Walking as fast as her condition would permit*\]

My girl, overpowered with drink as I am, my heart hastens me to see my lord. But my feet do not move along the path.

 **Nipu.—** We have already reached the swing-house.

 **Irā.— **Nipuṇikā, I do not see my lord here.

 **Nipu— **My lady, please look round. His Lordship may be in hiding somewhere out of fun. Let us also get to the stoneslab under the Aśoka tree, surrounded by the Priyamgu creeper.

***Page 33.***

 **Irā— **\[*Does so*\]

 **Nipu.—** (*Seeing*) Look here, my lady. While making a search for the mango-blossom, we have been stung by red ants !

 **Irā.—** How so ?

 **Nipu.—** Here is Bakulāvalikā completing the decoration of Mālavikā's feet under the shade of the Aśoka tree.

 **Ira.— **\[*Showing suspicion*). This is not the place for Mālavikā. What do you guess about it?

 ** Nipu.—** I think that Mālavikā has been assigned the duty of fulfilling the longing of the Aśoka tree by the queen whose foot is aching on account of a fall from the swing. Otherwise how could the queen permit her attendant to use the pair of anklets worn by herself?

 **Irā.— **Great indeed is the honour done to her.

 **Nipu.—** But why don't you search for his lordship?

 **Irā.—** My girl, my feet do not move further. My mind makes me very suspicious. I shall first remove my suspicions. \[*Looking at Mālavikā closely, aside*\] Rightly was my heart afraid.

***Page 34.***

 **Bakul.— **\[*Showing the foot to Mālavikā*\]. Do you liket his manner of painting?

 **Māla.—** As it is on mine own foot, I feel shy to praise it. Who gave you training in the art of decoration?

 ** Bakul.— **In this I am the pupil of his lordship.
