 The story of the play is the product of the fertile brain of the poet himself. It has, however, a historical background. The hero Agnimitra and his father Pushpamitra are historical personages. They belong to the Śunga dynasty of rulers who came into power after the Maurya Kings of Magadha. Brihaddratha, the last Maurya King, was slain in 178 B. C. by his Commander-in-Chief Pushpamitra who founded the Śunga dynasty. Soon after he put his son Agnimitra on the throne and himself preferred to retain the title of Senāpati.' Agnimitra had his capital at Vidiśā corresponding to the modern Bhilsa in Scindia's territory in Central India. The defeat of the king of Vidarbha (the modern Berars) and the performance of the horse-sacrifice by Pushpamitra are traditional even if not of historic authenticity. Vasumitra, the son of Agnimitra, is also a historical personage. Vahatava, Agnimitra's minister; Vīrasena, Agnimitra's brother-in law! Yajñasena, the king of Vidarbha; Mādhavasena, the cousin of Yajñasena; Sumati, Mādhavasena's minister; Kauśiki, Sumati's sister; Mālavikā, perhaps a princess of Mālava country, are also probably historical. The rest of the characters in the play are fictitious.

 The scene of action in the play is confined to Central India. The river Narmada can be regarded as the southern limit of the territory of Agnimitra. The kingdom of Vidarbha was situated to the south of this river. The river Varada, a tributary of the river Godāvarī, corresponds to the modern Wardha and divided the kingdom of Vidarbha into two equal parts which were given to Yajñasena and Mādhavasena. The Sindhu river probably formed the northern limit of Agnimitra's dominion, and the defeat of the Yavanas on its bank by Vasumitra probably refers to the defeat of a part of the army of Menander. It is to be noted that the Sindhu is not to be regarded as the Indus but as one of the tributaries of Jumna, that divided Bundelkhand from the Rajputana States.

**4. State of society as depicted in the drama.**

 Polygamy was prevalent among the princes King Agnimitra, the hero of the play, had already two wives. But he could contemplate having a third wife with equanimity and without the least hesitation or scruple of conscience. It is, however, to be remembered that polygamy is a recognized custom of the Hindu society and that there is not even the shadow of suggestion of any taint of immorality or impurity in the character of the hero. Chivalry and courtesy towards the fair sex were the common rule. The women on the other hand were devoted and obedient to their husbands. Seclusion of women was not in vogue.

 The king was guided by his ministers in all matters of administration, home or foreign, though his opinion carried great weight with the cabinet. It can therefore be inferred that the system of government prevailing was constitutional, and not absolute monarchy. The king was religious-minded and honoured the Brahmanas and the sages.

 Kālidāsa was a court-poet and graphically describes court-life with its intrigues. It seems that India was rich, prosperous and well-governed, though it was divided into a number of petty kingdoms. Trade was flourishing, though robbers were not altogether unknown. Literature and arts found favour in high society and had royal patronage. The play is full of references to dancing, music, painting and art in general. Teaching was regarded as a noble profession. Vedas and other religious literature formed part of the general studies. The science of medicine was well advanced. References to Dhruvasiddhi, a court-physician and poison-specialist, and the mention of remedies for a snake-bite, which hold even to-day, amply bear it out. Astrology was popular and astrologers commanded respect and authority. The Parivrājikā believes in and acts upon the prophecy of of a Sādhu about Mālavikā.

 The play depicts a flexible state of Hindu society. Buddhism had not completely disappeared from the land and was still held in esteem, but Hinduism had again come into its own. Kauśiki, the Buddhist nun, enjoyed universal respect and was always addressed as 'the revered lady', 'the learned lady' etc. Agrimitra himself justifies the putting on of the robes of an ascetic by Kauśiki with the remark 'युक्तः सज्जनस्यैष पन्थाः'.

**5. The Principal Characters.**

** Agnimitra.** King Agnimitra, the hero of the play, is portrayed with the artistic skill peculiar to a consummate artist like Kālidāsā. He is most vividly depicted as a lover. His love for Mālavikā is passionate without being degenerate, intense without being unrestrained, overpowering without being reckless. In his wooing he shows himself a perfect gentleman. He never exercises his authority as a king to further his suit. As a matter of fact, before courting Mālavikā he wants to be sure that his love is returned. Again, he takes care not to wound the feelings of his queen. Though he is pining for the love of Mālavikā, he does not woo her openly lest he should offend Dhāriṇī and Irāvatī. The latter insults and upbraids him, but he falls at her feet This courtsey towards his wives is one of the principal traits of his character. When he is taken to task by Mālavikā for being afraid of Irāvatī, he says that courtesy is his family vow. He has a beautiful sense of propriety. He would accept Mālavikā, only when her hand is offered to him by Dhāriṇī herself after she has conferred the title of 'queen' on her.

 The king has a keen and aesthetic sense of the beautiful in human form as well as in nature. His descriptions of nature and emotional moods are graphic but free from the least suggestion of licence. He has a great regard for womanhood and appreciates women for their culture as much as for their beauty. He considers that love to be highest when its flame burns alike in the hearts of two persons, even though they may not be united.

 Had it not been for the fine setting of political and national life for the hero, the love motif in the play would have degenerated to the level of a common court intrigue. As a king, he was learned in theoretical statecraft as well as expert in the art of practical government. He has respect for constitutional government. In all matters pertaining to the state he acts with the consultation of his ministers. The declaration of war against Yajṅasena shows his political sagacity. The policy of dividing the kingdom equally between the two cousins, Yajňasena and Mādhavasena, after victory proves his generosity towards the vanquished foe and his acquaintance with the political maxim 'divide and rule.' Though he is busy in love-making, his ministers and generals under his watchful eye give a good account of themselves.The epilogue shows that he is sure that natural calamities will not visit his subjects during his reign.

 He has great regard for Buddhism, as is evident from his remark ‘सज्जनस्यैष पन्थाः' to Kauśiki when she announces that she put on the orange-coloured robes of an ascetic on entering his kingdom.

 Some critics in their prudishness have dubbed Agnimitra as a voluptuary. The charge is as baseless as it is reckless and does not need even a refutation.

 **Mālavikā.** Mālavikā, really a princess of Vidarbha but shown in the drama till almost the end as an attendant of queen Dhāriṇī, is the heroine. Her character is painted subtly with faint but effective touches of the brush. She is an innocent, pure-minded, unsophisticated girl young in years but endowed with gifts. She is an uncommon beauty. The king loses his heart to her on seeing her in the picture. She adds accomplishments and talents to her good looks. She pleases her tutor as a pupil who is intelligent, and quick to learn, and strikes her as one coming of a noble lineage. She delights all with her exquisite dancing.

 She possesses dignity. She falls in love with the king, but does not betray her secret except to Bakulāvalikā, her friend, and that too only when the latter reveals to her the king's love for her. Her simplicity is shown when she gets angry with the king in his picture. At the king's remark that she has no need to be afraid of Irāvati, she reminds him how such a brave person behaved sometime before in her presence. This shows her naive wit. She is, however, no match for the older and more experienced Bakulāvalikā in conversation and allows herself to be drawn out by the latter during their conversation in the pleasure-garden.

 She has patience and self-command. Though she is a princess, she never complains of her position as a servant. She respects and fears Dhāriṇi. Being young, she is naturally timid. She is afraid of serpents. The mention of robbers makes her tremble.

 She has a tender heart and is of an amiable, sweet and affectionate disposition. When she stretches her foot for being painted by Bakulāvalikā, she begs pardon of the latter for her impudence in doing so. In short, she is a most lovely and lovable person, of a type quite different from Dhāriṇi and Irāvatī.

 ** Dhāriṇī.** ** **Dhāriṇī is portrayed as an ideal Indian wife who considers the happiness of her husband to be her chief concern and who is attached to him, her children and her attendants. She is the chief queen and behaves with grace, dignity and magnanimity as befits her age and position. She is an elderly lady, as is evident from the fact that she has a son, prince Vasumitra, who is in charge of the horse let loose by Puśpamitra to roam unfettered for the purpose of performing the horse-sacrifice. Her conduct throughout is typical of a lady advanced in years. Self-control and forgiveness are the main traits of her character. The name Dhāriṇī, itself suggests the same. The Parivrājikā speaks of her as being as forgiving as the Earth itself.

 The king has the highest regard for her feelings and makes it one of the main concerns of his life to please her. She is a devoted and faithful wife and, despite just cause for anger, overlooks and forgives the king's faults.

 As she has control over her feelings, she never yields to fits of jealousy and temper like Irāvatī. She is not suspicious by nature and readily believes in what she sees or hears. She is taken in by the ruse of the snake-bite and hands over her signet ring, little suspecting the use to which it would be put. Considerate as she is to her attendants, she treats Mālavikā with respect. She puts her and Bakulāvalikā in fetters only to please Irāvatī.

 She is charitable and religious-minded. For her son's victory she offers prayers and daily distributes money among the deserving. She is respectful towards the Parivrājikā.

 She is not altogether lacking in shrewdness. She sees through the king's game in the quarrel between Hardatta and Gaṇadāsa and tells him that it would bring him greater glory if he were to take as much interest in affairs of the state as he did in affairs of the heart.

 She is loyal to her word and is generous. She promises to Mālavikā that she would fulfil her wish if the Aśoka tree blossoms within five nights of the kick. She keeps her word and in presenting Mālavikā to the king herself and conferring the title of 'queen' on her shows her generosity also.

 To use the words of the poet, she is a 'वीरपत्नी' ('the wife of a hero') and a 'वीरस्नू' ('the mother of a hero').

 **Irāvatī.** Irāvatī is depicted as a fine contrast to Dhāriṇī. She is young, passionate, impetuous and impulsive, and is flushed with her youth, loveliness and wine. As the junior queen, she is the favourite of the king before Mālavikā's appearance on the scene. She is suspicious, jealous and hot-tempered and is therefore less disposed than Dhāriṇī to overlook the faults of the king. She smells an intrigue everywhere and has recourse to constant eaves-dropping. She is provoked quickly but takes long to forgive. In her fit of jealousy she forgets herself as well as her husband's rank and rights. On finding him with Mālavikā she insults. him and gets ready to beat him with her girdle and does not forgive him even when he falls at her feet.

 She is, however, shrewd. Both the king and the Vidūshaka do not succeed in throwing dust into her eyes. 'निसर्गनिपुणाः स्त्रियः' 'fits her aptly. She again shows this natural shrewdness in bowing to the inevitable and sending to the king a message for forgiveness and reconciliation on the king's marriage with Mālavikā.

 ** Kauśiki**. Kauśiki is delineated as a Buddhist nun (परिव्राजिका). But she is not represented as an ascetic holding life and human beings in contempt but as one full of 'the milk of human kindness.'

 She has lost her husband in her early age but she is reconciled to her condition. When, however, her brother is killed in an engagement with robbers while trying to protect Mālavikā, his master's sister, she feels the grief of widowhood revived and puts on the robes of an ascetic. Still she does not retire from life but attaches herself to the queen Dhāriṇī in the court of Agnimitra and there allies herself with the Vidūshaka, the king's friend and confidant, as her one ambition in life is to see Mālavikā accepted as the king's wife.

 She is forbearing, resourceful and learned. She is quite conversant with the theory and practice of dancing. She is an expert in decoration. She is no less proficient in the science of medicine. The remedies she suggests for the snake-bite hold true even to-day. She is a good story-teller and is sought by Dhāriṇi to divert her.

 She has great faith in astrology and believes in the Sādhu's prophecy about Mālavikā being united with a suitable husband after one year's servitude. She shows her patience, prudence and foresight in that she sees Mālavikā at the palace but does not disclose her identity at once.

 She has an attendant of her own in the palace and is treated with respect and reverence by all. She is always addressed as 'the revered lady', 'the learned Kauśiki,' etc.

 She is very happy on the marriage of Mālavikā with the king. She has the delicate tact to offer to go to Mādhavasena on the consummation of the happy event, but is also amiable enough to accede to the request of the king and the queen to stay with them.

 **Bakulāvalikā.** Bakulāvalikā is to Mālavikā what the Vidūshaka is to Agnimitra. A maid-servant of the queen Dhāriṇī, she is probably attracted by Mālavikā's beauty, charms and accomplishments and becomes her friend. She is taken into confidence by the Vidūshaka and the two help each other to bring Mālavikā and the king together. Bakulāvalikā is clever and shrewd. In her talk with Mālavikā in the pleasure-garden, she so dexterously draws out of Mālavikā's lips her avowal of love for the king and at the same time appraises her of the king's love for her. She is adept as a female messenger and does not mind hardships in the execution of her mission. She is thrown into prison along with Mālavikā , but she persists in her task of accomplishing a union between the hero and the heroine.

 She is very good at pleasant repartee. When Mālavikā begs for her forgiveness for stretching out her foot, she says, "you are my very self." When Mālavikā asks her to stand by her in her difficulty, she replies with a pun on her own name, "Bakulāvalikā (the garland of Bakula flowers) is all the more fragrant when it is rubbed." She is really 'विमर्दसुरभिर्नकुलावलिकाः'

 **Vidūshaka.** Gautama, the Jester is depicted in the play not only in his usual traits—a great glutton, always fond of

**APPENDIX III**

**DRAMATURGICAL TERMS**

 1. **नान्दी** or 'Benediction'. *'Nandi*' is a benedictory verse recited in the beginning of the play. It serves a double purpose. It contains the praise of a Deity, a Brahmaṇa, a king, or the like, combined with a benediction in favour of the audience. Sometimes it suggests the subject-matter of the play also.

 2. **सूत्रधारः** or 'Stage-manager'. The *'Sūtra-dhára'* is the stage-manager or the director of the play. He superintends the whole performance. The word literally means 'thread-holder'— the principal actor who 'holds the thread' of the drama *i.e*., directs the stage-business. According to some he was originally so called from holding the strings of puppets. He introduces the play and its author and acquaints the audience with the starting point of the story.

 3. **प्रस्तावना** or 'Prologue'. The '*Prastávaná'* is the prologue at the commencement of every Sanskrit drama. It is an introductory dialogue between the stage-manager and an actress, or his assistant, or the jester on a matter of his own and hinting at or bringing in the matter to be represented. It introduces the play, the author and the starting point of the story. It is also designated स्थापना or आमुख.

 4. **नेपथ्य** or the 'Tiring-room'. The 'nepathya' is the 'tiring-room' or the room behind the principal curtain where the actors attire themselves and remain in readiness to enter the stage.

 **Note—**'नेपथ्ये' as a stage-direction in the drama means 'behind the scenes', नेपथ्य also means 'decoration, toilet, costume (especially of an actor), attire.

 5. **विष्कम्भक** or 'Interlude'. The *'Vishkambhaka'* is an interlude at the beginning of an act of a play enacted by minor characters *i.e*., मध्यम or middling and नीच or low ones, who by their conversation briefly indicate parts of the story both past and future. It is शुद्ध or pure when performed by one or more of middling characters, मिश्र or mixed when performed by both middling and low characters. It is necessary for acquainting the audience with incidents which are not actually represented on the stage but the knowledge of which is necessary for the proper understanding of the plot.

 The language to be used in a विष्कम्भक is either Sanskrit or Sanskrit and Prākrita. In शुद्ध विष्कम्भक the conversation is carried on entirely in Sanskrit, while in a मिश्र or सङ्कीर्ण विष्कम्भक it is done both in Sanskrit and Prākrita.

 6. **प्रवेशक** or 'Interlude. The *'Praveśaka'* is an interlude performed between two consecutive acts by one or two low characters in discourse not very dignified. It is intended like the Vishkambhaka to connect the parts of the story by briefly referring to what has occurred in the interval or what is going to happen subsequently.

 The language to be used in a प्रवेशक Prākrita only.

 ***Note—*** The main points of difference between a विष्कम्भक and प्रवेशक are :—

| | |
|:--:|:--:|
| **विष्कम्भक** | **प्रवेशक** |
| 1\. Middling or middling and low characters take part | 1\. Only low characters take part |
| 2\. The dialogue is in Sanskrit or both Sanskrit and Prākrita. | 2\. The dialogue is entirely in Prākrita |
| 3\. Vishkambhaka may come at the beginning of the first act of a play. | 3\. Praveśaka can find a the place only between two acts. |

 In all other respects विष्कम्भक and प्रवेशक are similar. Both are intended for brevity. Both indicate past and future events.

 7. **भरतवाक्यम्** or 'Epilogue'. The *'Bharata-Vakya'* is the technical name given to the last verse or verses of a play and is so called in honour of the Sage Bharata, the founder of Sanskrit Dramaturgy. It is a sort of benediction containing an expression of general peace and goodwill and is recited, pronounced, sung by an actor or all the actors jointly. It literally means 'speech of Bharata'.

 8. **प्रकाशम्** or 'Aloud'. 'Prakaśam' is a stage-direction with regard to a speech which may be heard by all and corresponds to the 'Aloud' of the English drama.

 9. **आत्मगतम्** or 'Aside'. 'Atmagatam' is a stage-direction with regard to a speech which is not to be heard by anybody or is spoken to oneself and corresponds to the 'Aside' of the English drama. स्वगतम् is also used in the same sense. 'आत्मगतम्' and 'स्वगतम्' both literally means 'to oneself'.

 10. **अपवारितम्** or "'Aside' to another person". "Apavarya' is a stage-direction with' regard to a speech intended to be heard by the addressed person only. 'अपवारितेन' 'अपवारितनके' and जनान्तकम् are all used in the same sense.

 11. **जनान्तिकम्** or "'Aside'. 'जनान्तिकम्'' is a stage-direction with regard to a speech by way of mutual whisper between two persons in the midst of the conversation of the company, preventing, as it were, the others from hearing by means of the three-bannered hand.

 ***Note.—*** 'Three-bannered' hand implies the hand raised in the form of the 'three bannered' *i.e*., with all the fingers raised but the ring-finger lowered.

 12. **परिपार्श्विक** or 'Assistant'. The 'Pāriparśvika' is an assistant of the manager of a play. He is one of the interlocutors in the prologue. The word literally means 'one who stands by the side' of the Sūtradhāra.

 13. **भाव**. In dramatical language 'Bhāva' is used as a term of address for the Sūtradhāra. It may be rendered into English by 'Sir.'

 14. **मारिष.— **In dramatic language 'Māriśha' is used as term of address for the Pāriparṣvika. It may be rendered into English by 'my dear sir.' The word literally means 'a respectable person, a venerable man.'

 ***Note.—*** The Sutradhāra is a superior, and the Pariparśvika is his inferior. The Sutradhāra is to address the Pāriparśvika as 'Mariśha,' and the Pāriparśvika should address the Sutradhāra as 'Bhava'.

 15. **विदूषक** for 'Jester'. The 'Vidūshaka' is the jester whose business, as a rule, is to help the hero in the accomplishment of his object and to cheer him up. He is invariably a Brahmaṇa, a constant companion and confidant of the hero. He is generally noted for his great hunger and ready wit. He is expected to excite mirth by his quaint actions, speeches, person and dress etc., and to delight in squabbles. In short, he plays the part of a buffoon in a drama. The word literally means 'a jester, a joker.'

 16. **कञ्चुकी** or 'Chamberlain'. The 'Kaṇchuki,' so called from the long cloak (कञ्चुकी) worn by him, is the chief attendant of the harem. He is represented as an aged Brāhmaṇa of irreproachable character and possessed of a number of virtues such as truthfulness etc. He is an adept in all the affairs of the harem. The word literally means 'an attendant of women's apartments', a chamberlain.

 17. **आर्यपुत्र**. In drama 'Arya-putra' is a term of address for the husband by the wife. The word literally means 'the son of the honoured one', *i.e.*, the father-in-law. It may be rendered into English by 'my lord.'

**APPENDIX IV**

**DRAMATIS PERSONÆ**

***Males***

** सूत्रधारः—** The stage-manager.

** पारिपार्श्विकः—** The assistant of the Sutradhāra.

** राजा (अग्निमित्रः**)**— **The hero, the king of Vidiśā.

** विदूषकः (गौतमः)— **The jester, personal friend and confidant of the king.

** अमात्यः (वाक्ष्तवः)—** A minister of Agnimitra.

** हरदत्तः— **A master of dance attached to the court and patronised by the king.

** गणदासः— **Another master of dance attached to the court, a rival of **हरदत्त** and patronised by the queen.

** कञ्चुकी (मौद्गल्यः)— **The Chamberlain.

** सारसिकः—** A hunchback, attendant of queen Dhāriṇi.

** वैतालिकः—** A bard attached to the court.

 Male attendants.

*Females*

** मालविका—**The heroine, a princess of Vidarbha and the sister of prince Mādhavasena.

** धारिणी (देवी)— **The chief queen and the wife of Agnimitra.

** इरावती— **The other queen, junior to Dhāriṇi and another wife of Agnimitra.

** परिव्राजिका (कैशिकि)— **A Buddhist nun, attached to Dhāriṇi's court.

** प्रतीहारी (जयसेना)—** The door-keeper of the palace.

** बकुलावलिका— **A maid-servant of queen Dhāriṇi and an intimate friend of Mālavikā.

** कौमुदिका— **A maid-servant of Dhāriṇi.

** नागरिका— **Another maid-servant of Dhāriṇi.

** निपुणिका— **A maid-servant of Irāvatī.

** समाहितिका— **A maid-servant of the Parivrājikā.

** उद्यानपालिका (मधुकरिका)—** The garden-keeper of the pleasure-garden.

** ज्योत्स्निका—** An artist maid sent as a present by Yajñsena, the prince of Vidarbha, to king Agnimitra.

** मदनिका— **Another artist maid sent as a present-by Yajñasena, the prince of Vidarbha, to king Agnimitrā.

 Female attendants.

**Other Persons mentioned in the play.**

** यज्ञसेन—** The king of the Vidarbhas.

** माधवसेन—** A cousin of Yajñasena, and the brother of Mālavikā.

** सुमति—** A minister of Mādhavasena

** पुश्पमित्र—** Father of Agnimitra.

** वसुमित्र—** Son of Agnimitra.

** वीरसेन— **The brother of queen Dhāriṇi.

** मौर्यसचिव—** 'The minister of the Mauryas', the brother-in-law of Yajñasena.

** ध्रुवसिद्धि— **A court physician, a specialist in poisons.

** वसुलक्ष्मी— **The little princess, the sister of queen Dhāriṇī.

** माधविका— **A maid-servant, keeper of the under-ground cell.

** चन्द्रिका— **A maid-servant of Irāvatī.

| **अप्याकरसमुत्पन्ना** | **क्व रुजा हृदयप्रमाथिनी** |
| **अर्थं सप्रतिबन्धं** | **चरणान्तनिवेशितां** |
| **अलमन्यथा गृहीत्वा** | **चित्रगतायामस्यां** |
| **अव्याजसुन्दरीं तां** | **छेदो दंशस्य दाहो वा** |
| **अहं रथाङ्गनामेव** | **जनभिममनुरक्तं** |
| **आदाय कर्णकिसलय** | **जीमूतस्तनिताविशाङ्कि** |
| **आमत्तान्ना श्रवणसुभगैः** | **ततः परान्पराजित्य** |
| **आर्द्रालक्तकमस्या॰** | **तामाश्रित्य श्रुतिपथ॰** |
| **इमां परीप्सुर्दुर्जाते** | **तूणीरपट्टपरिणद्ध॰** |
| **इष्टाधिगमनिमित्तं** | **तौ पृथग्वरदाकूले** |
| **उचितः प्रणयो वरं** | **त्वदुपलभ्य समीपगतां** |

———————————————————————————————

| | |
|--------------------------|--------------------------|
| **त्वं मे प्रसादसुमुखी** | **भ्रूभङ्गभिन्नतिलकं** |
| **दाक्षिण्यं नाम बिम्बोष्टि** | **मङ्गलालङ्कृता भान्ति** |
| **दीर्घाक्षं शरदिन्दुकान्ति** | **मधुरस्वरा परभृता** |
| **दुर्लभः प्रियस्तस्मिन्भव** | **मन्दोऽप्यमन्दतां** |
| **देवानामिदमामनान्ति** | **मन्ये प्रियाहृतमनाः** |
| **द्वारे नियुक्तपुरुषा॰** | **महासारप्रसवयोः** |
| **द्विधा विभक्तां श्रिय॰** | **मामियमभ्युत्तिष्ठति** |
| **धृतिपुष्पमयमपि** | **मौर्यसचिवं विमुञ्चति** |
| **धैर्यावलम्बिनमपि** | **यद्यत्प्रयोगविषये** |
| **न च न परिचितो** | **रक्ताशोकरुचां विशेषित॰** |
| **नवकिसलयरागेण॰** | **लब्धास्पदोऽस्मीति** |
| **न हि बुद्धिगुणेनैव** | **वामं सन्धिस्तिमितवलयं** |
| **नायं देव्या भाजनत्वं** | **विपुलं नितम्बबिम्बे** |
| **नार्हति कृतापराधो** | **विरचितपदं वीरप्रीत्या** |
| **नेपथ्यपरिगताया॰** | **विवादे दर्शयिष्यन्तं** |
| **नैतावता वीरविजृम्भि॰** | **विसृज सुन्दरि सङ्गम॰** |
| **पत्रच्छायासु हंसा** | **वोढा कुरबकरजसां** |
| **पथि नयनयोः स्थित्वा** | **शठ इति मयि तावदस्तु** |
| **परभृतकलव्याहारेषु** | **शरकाण्डपाण्डुगण्ड॰** |
| **पात्रविशेषे न्यस्तं** | **शरीरं क्षामं स्यादसति** |
| **पुराणमित्येव न साधु॰** | **शिरसा प्रथमगृहीतां** |
| **प्रतिपक्षेणापि पतिं** | **शिष्टा क्रिया कस्यचिदा॰** |
| **प्रेष्यभावेन नामेयं** | **सर्वान्तः पुरवनिता॰** |
| **बाष्पासारा हेमकाञ्ची॰** | **सर्वाशोकतरूणां** |
| **भर्त्रासि वीरपत्नीनां** | **सूर्योदये भवति या** |
| **भाग्यास्तमयमिवाक्ष्णोः** | **स्मयमानमायताक्ष्याः** |
| **भावज्ञानानन्तर॰** | **हस्तं कम्पवती रुणद्धि** |

APPENDIX VI

THE SUBHASHITAS OCCURRING IN THE PLAY

**1. Sentences.**

| |
|-------------------------------------------------------|
| **अनुरागोऽनुरागेण परीक्षितव्यः।** |
| **अन्योन्यकलहितयोर्मत्तहस्तिनोरेकतरस्मिन्ननिर्जिते कुत उपशमः** |
| **अपरिनिष्टितस्योपदेशस्यान्याय्यं प्रकाशनम्।** |
| **अपर्वणि ग्रहकलुषेन्दुमण्डला विभावरी कथय कथं भविष्यति।** |
| **अहो अविश्वसनीयाः पुरुषाः।** |
| **अहो दुरासदो राजमहिमा।** |
| **अहो परिभवोपहारिणो विनिपाताः।** |
| **अहो सर्वस्थानानवद्यता (सर्वास्ववस्थास्वान॰) रूपस्य।** |
| **अहो सर्वास्ववस्थासु चारुता शोभां (शोभान्तरं) पुष्यति।** |
| **आकृतिविशेषेष्वादरः पदं करोति।** |
| **आगामि सुखं दुःखं वा हृदयसमवस्थां कथयतीति।** |
| **इयं खलु सीधुपानोद्वेजितस्या मत्स्यण्डिकोपनता।** |
| **उचितवेलातिक्रमे चिकित्सका दोषमुदाहरन्ति।** |
| **उपस्थितं नयनमधु सन्निहितमक्षिकं च।** |
| **कर्मगृहीतेन कुम्भीलकेन सन्धिच्छेदे शिक्षितोऽस्मीति वक्तव्यं भवति!** |
| **कातरो बालभावः।** |
| **कामं खलु सर्वस्यापि कुलविद्या बहुमता।** |
| **किं नु खलु दर्दुरा व्याहरन्तीति देवः प्रथिवीं विस्मरति।** |
| **कुतूहलवानपि निसर्गशालीनः स्त्रीजनः।** |
| **कुम्भीलकैः कामुकैश्च परिहरणीया खलु चन्द्रिका।** |
| **चन्दनं खलु पादुकोपयोगेन (ºकापरिभोगेण) दूषितम्।** |
| **चूताङ्कुरं विचिन्वत्योः पिपीलिकाभिर्दष्टम्।** |
| **दंशच्छेदः पूर्वकर्म।** |

———————————————————————————————

| |
|---------------------------------------------------------|
| **न च प्रियेष्वायतलोचनानां समग्रपातीनि विलोचनानि।** |
| **न चापि काव्यं नवमित्यवद्यम्।** |
| **न शोभते प्रणयिनि जने निरपेक्षता।** |
| **न हि कमलिनीं दृष्ट्वा ग्राहमवेक्षते मतङ्गजः।** |
| **नाट्यं भिन्नरुचेर्जनस्य बहुधाप्येकं समाराधनम्।** |
| **निसर्गनिपुणाः स्त्रियः।** |
| **पण्डितपरितोषप्रत्यया ननु मूढा जातिः।** |
| **पतने विद्यमानेऽपि ग्रामे रत्नपरीक्षा।** |
| **प्रभवत्याचार्यः शिष्यजनस्य।** |
| **प्रभवन्त्योऽपि हि भर्तृषु कारणकोपाः कुटुम्बिन्यः।** |
| **प्रयोगप्रधानं हि नाट्यशास्त्रम्** |
| **प्रायः समानविद्याः परस्परयशः पुरोभागाः।** |
| **बन्धनभ्रष्टो गृहकपोतोश्चिल्लाया मुखे (बिडालिकालोके) पतितः।** |
| **भ्रमरसम्बाध इति वसन्तावतारसर्वस्वं किं न चूतप्रसवोऽवतंसयितव्यः।** |
| **\[मदः किल स्त्रीजनस्य विशेषमण्डनम्।\]** |
| **मया नाम मुग्धचातकेनेव शुष्कवनगर्जितेऽन्तरिक्षे जलपानमिष्टम्।** |
| **महत्खलु पुरुषाकारमिदं ज्योतिः।** |
| **मूढः परप्रत्ययनेयबुद्धिः।** |
| **मृदु तीक्ष्णतरं यदुच्यते तदिदं मन्मथ दृश्यते त्वयि।** |
| **यस्यागमः केवलजीविकायै तं ज्ञानपण्यं वणिजं वदन्ति।** |
| **रमणीयः खलु नवाङ्गनानां मदनविषयव्यापारः।** |
| **विनेतुरद्रव्यपरिग्रहोऽपि बुद्धिलाघवं प्रकाशयति।** |
| **विपणिगत इव बलीवर्द आसीन एव निद्रायते।** |
| **सन्तः परीज्ञ्यान्यतरद्भजन्ते।** |
| **सर्वज्ञस्याप्येकाकिनो निर्णयाभ्युपगमो दोषाय।** |
| **सर्वोऽपि नववरो लज्जातुरो भवति।** |
| **साधु त्वं दरिद्र इवातुरो वैद्येनोपनीयमानमौषधमिच्छसि।** |
| **सुशिक्षितोऽपि न सर्व उपदेशदर्शने न निपुणो भवति।** |
| **सूनापरिसरचरो विहङ्गम इवामिपलोलुपो भीरुकश्च।** |
| **स्थाने प्राणाः कामिनां दूत्यधीनाः।** |

————————————

**2. Slokas.**

**अचिराधिष्टितराज्यः शत्रुः प्रकृतिष्वरूढमूलत्वात्।  
नवसंरोपणशिथिलस्तरुरिव सुकरः समुद्धर्तुम्॥**

**अतिमात्रभासुरत्वं पुष्यति भानोः परिग्रहादनलः।  
अधिगच्छति महिमानं चन्द्रोऽपि निशापरिगृहीतः॥**

**अनातुरोत्कण्ठितयोः प्रसिध्यता समागमेनापिरतिर्न मां प्रति।  
परस्परप्राप्तिनिराशयोर्वरं शरीरनाशोऽपि समानुरागयोः॥**

**अप्याकरसमुत्पन्ना मणिजातिरसंस्कृता।  
जातरूपेण कल्याणि न हि संयोगमर्हति॥**

**अथ सप्रतिबन्धं प्रभुरधिगन्तुं सहायवानेव।  
दृश्यं तमसि न पश्यति दीपेन विना सचक्षुरपि॥**

**उपदेशं विदुः शुद्धं सन्तस्तमुपदेशिनः।  
श्यामायते न विद्वत्सु यः काञ्चनमिवाग्निषु॥**

**छेदो दंशस्य दाहो वा क्षतेर्वा रक्तमोक्षणम्।  
एतानि दष्टमात्राणामायुष्याः प्रतिपत्तयः॥**

**न हि बुद्धिगुणेनैव सुहृदामर्थदर्शनम्।  
कार्यसिद्धिपथः सूक्ष्मः स्नेहेनाप्युपलभ्यते॥**

**पात्रविशेषे न्यस्तं गुणान्तरं व्रजति शिल्पमाधातुः।  
जलमिव समुद्रशुक्तौ मुक्ताफलतां पयोदस्य॥**

**पुराणमित्येव न साधु सर्वं न चापि काव्यं नवमित्यवद्यम्।  
सन्तः परीक्ष्यान्यतरद्भजन्ते मूढः परप्रत्ययनेयबुद्धिः॥**

**प्रतिपक्षेणापि पतिं सेवन्ते भर्तृवत्सलाः साध्व्यः।  
अन्यसरितां शतानि हि समुद्रगाः प्रापयन्त्यब्धिम्॥**

**मन्दोऽप्यमन्दतामेति संसर्गेण विपश्चितः।  
पङ्कच्छिदः फलस्येव निकषेणाविलं पयः॥**

**लब्धास्पदोऽस्मीति विवादभीरोस्तितिक्षमाणस्य परेण निन्दाम्।  
यस्यागमः केवलजीविकायै तं ज्ञानपण्यं वणिजं वरन्ति॥**

**शिष्टा क्रिया कस्यचिदात्मसंस्था सङ्क्रान्तिरन्यस्य विशेषयुक्ता।  
यस्योभयं साधु स शिक्षकाणा धुंरि प्रतिष्ठापयितव्य एव॥**

\(e\) देव अयमेव मयि प्रथमं परिवादकरः। अत्रभवतः किल मम च समुद्रपल्वलयोरिवान्तरभिति। तदत्रभवानिमं मां च शास्त्रे प्रयोगे च विमृशतु। देव एव नौ विशेषज्ञः प्राश्निकः।

 III. Explain with reference to the context *any three* of the following, and render the two Prākrit passages into Sanskrit :―

\(a\) चित्रगतायामस्यां कान्तिसंवादशङ्कि मे हृदयम्।

\(b\) कार्यसिद्धिपथः सूक्ष्मः स्रेहेनाप्युपलभ्यते।

\(c\) वीरसूरितिशब्दोयं तनयात् त्वामुपस्थितः।

\(d\) सुदं भवदा। अत्तहोदी चित्ते जह दिठ्ठो तह ण दिठ्ठो भवं ति मन्तेदि। मुहा दाणिं मञ्जूसा विअ रअणभण्डअं जोव्वणगव्वं वहेसि।

\(e\) विस्ससणीओसि। मए ण विण्णादम् ईरिसं विणोदवत्यु अज्जउत्तेण उवलद्धतिम्। अण्णाहा मन्दभाइणीए एव्वं ण करीअदि।                        
           **9,4**

 IV. How was Mālavikā rescued from the underground cell where she had been imprisoned by the queen ?                    
                    **5**

 V. Translate into Sanskrit :—                   
                 **35**

**1936-Supplementary**

 I. Translate into English *any four* of the following:—

\(a\) Act II, verse 14 (b) Act III, verse 18

\(c\) Act IV, verse 2 (d) Act V, verse 13

\(e\) इदानीमेव पञ्चाङ्गाभिनयमुपदिश्य मया विश्रम्यतामित्यभिहिता दीर्घिकावलोकनगवाक्षगता प्रवातमासेवमाना तिष्ठति।

\(f\) सोऽहमिदानीमुंशुमतेव सगरः पौत्रेण प्रत्याहृताश्वो यक्ष्ये। तदिदानीमकालहीनं विगतरोषचेतसा भवता वधूजनेन सह यज्ञसेवनायागन्तव्यमिति।           
** 16**

Act I, verse 5.                            
                 **5**

 III. Explain. with reference to the context, *any three* of the following, and render the two Prākrit passages into Sanskrit—

\(a\) विसृज सुन्दरि सङ्गमसाध्वसं तव चिरात्प्रभृति प्रणयोन्मुखे।

\(b\) मोक्ता माधवसेनं ततोहमपि बन्धनात्सद्यः।

\(c\) यस्यागमः केवलजीविकायै तं ज्ञानपण्यं वणिजं वदन्ति।

\(d\) भोदि जीवेअं वा ण वा। जं मए अत्तभवन्तं सेवमाणेण ते अवरद्धं तं मरिसेहि।

\(e\) जाणामि णिमित्तं कोदुअलङ्कारस्स। तन्ह वि बिसिणीपत्तगदं विअ सलिलं वेवदि मे हिअअम्। ** 9,4**

 I. Translate into English *any four* of the following :—

\(a\) Act III, verse 22 (b) Act III, verse 11

\(c\) Act II, verse 10 (d) Act V, verse 7

\(e\) विजयतां देवः। देव अमात्यो विज्ञापयति। तस्मिन् विदर्भविषयोपायने द्वे शिल्पकारिके मार्गपरिश्रमादलघुशरीरे इति पूर्वं न प्रवेशिते। सम्प्रति देवोपस्थानयोग्ये संवृत्ते। तदाज्ञां देवो दातुमर्हतीति।

\(f\) तक्केमि दोलापरिब्भट्ठाए सरुअचलणाए देवीए असोअदोहलाहिआरे मालविआ णिउत्तेति। अण्णहां कहं सअं धारिअण्णूउरजुलं परिअणस्स अणुजाणिस्सदि।

\(b\) स्थाने प्राणाः कामिनां दूत्यधीनाः।

\(c\) द्वारपिधानमिव धृतेर्मन्ये तस्यास्तिरस्करणम्।

\(d\) गौतम चिन्तेहि दाव उवाअम्। जहा मे जदिच्छादिठ्ठप्पकिदी मालविआ पच्चखदंसणा होदित्ति।

\(e\) का वअं भट्ठिणिं णिऔजेदु। परिअणणिअलणेण दंसिदो मइ अणुग्गहो।
